PREFACE
         This code of the City of New Plymouth, as supplemented, contains
ordinances up to and including ordinance 424, passed September 5, 2023.
Ordinances of the City adopted after said ordinance supersede the provisions of
this code to the extent that they are in conflict or inconsistent therewith.
Consult the City office in order to ascertain whether any particular provision
of the code has been amended, superseded or repealed.
               American Legal Publishing
               Cincinnati, Ohio
ORDINANCES PENDING REVIEW FOR CODIFICATION
Listed ordinances have been passed, but they are pending review by the
publisher, and they may not amend the code of ordinances. Additionally,
ordinances listed in this section may not show the original ordinances in their
entirety. Please contact the office of the clerk if there are any questions
concerning any listed ordinances.
ADOPTING ORDINANCE
AN ORDINANCE PROVIDING FOR THE ADOPTION AND OFFICIAL AND CONTINUOUS USE OF THE
MUNICIPAL CODE OF THE CITY OF NEW PLYMOUTH, IDAHO.
IT IS HEREBY ORDAINED BY THE MAYOR AND COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF NEW PLYMOUTH,
that:
Section 1. From and after the date of passage of this Ordinance the Municipal
Code of the City of New Plymouth, prepared by Sterling Codifiers and hereby
approved and accepted shall be the Official Code of all Ordinances of a general
and permanent character of the City.
Section 2. There is hereby adopted, as a method of perpetual codification, the
loose leaf type of binding together with the continuous supplemental service
whereby each newly adopted Ordinance of a general nature, amending, altering,
adding to, or deleting provisions of the Municipal Code is identified by the
proper catch line, and following preparation by Sterling Codifiers, is inserted
in the proper place in each of the official copies. Each such insertion shall
be made within thirty (30) days following the date of adoption by the Council,
and each new provision shall become effective upon such insertion.
Section 3. At least one (1) official copy of said official Municipal Code of
the City of New Plymouth shall at all times be on file and available for
inspection in the office of the Clerk.
This Ordinance passed by roll call vote of the City Council this fourth day of
January, 1960, and approved by the Mayor on this fourth day of January, 1960.
TITLE I
ADMINISTRATIVE
CHAPTER 1
ADOPTION OF OFFICIAL CODE
SECTION:
1-1-1: Title
1-1-2: Acceptance
1-1-3: Amendments
1-1-4: Construction of Words
1-1-5: Definitions
1-1-6: Interpretations
1-1-7: Penalties
1-1-8: Liability of Officers
1-1-1: TITLE:
This compilation and codification of the general ordinances of the City of New
Plymouth is hereby declared to be and shall hereafter constitute the official
Municipal Code of the City of New Plymouth. Any reference to the number of any
Section contained herein shall be understood to refer to the position of the
same under its appropriate Title heading, its Chapter heading, and its Section
heading, and to the general penalty clause relating thereto, as well as to the
Section itself, when reference is made in this Code by title in any legal
document.
1-1-2: ACCEPTANCE:
This Municipal Code of the City of New Plymouth, as hereby presented in printed
form, shall hereafter be received without further proof in all courts and in
all administrative tribunals of this State as the ordinances of a general and
permanent effect of the City.
1-1-3: AMENDMENTS:
Any ordinance amending this Code shall set forth the Title, Chapter and Section
number of the Section or Sections to be amended, and this shall constitute a
sufficient compliance with any statutory requirement pertaining to the
amendment or revision by ordinance of any part of this Code. All such
amendments or revisions by ordinance shall be immediately forwarded to the
codifiers and the said ordinance material shall be prepared for insertion in
its proper place in each copy of the Municipal Code. Each such replacement page
shall be properly identified and shall be inserted in each copy of the
Municipal Code within thirty (30) days from the date of its final passage.
1-1-4: CONSTRUCTION OF WORDS:
Whenever any word in any Section of this Municipal Code importing the plural
number is used, in describing or referring to any matters, parties, or persons,
any single matter, party, or person shall be deemed to be included, although
distributive words may not have been used.
When any subject matter, party, or person is referred to in this Municipal Code
by words importing the singular number only, or the masculine gender, several
matters, parties, or persons and females as well as males and bodies corporate
shall be deemed to be included. The word "person" shall be deemed to include
any "person, firm, association or corporation" or any organization of any kind.
The words, "written" and "in writing" may include printing. Provided, that
these rules of construction shall not be applied to any Section of the
Municipal Code which contains any express provision excluding such construction
or where the subject matter or content may be repugnant thereto.
1-1-5: DEFINITIONS:
The term "personal property" includes every description of money, goods,
chattels, effects, evidence of rights in action, and all written instruments by
which any pecuniary obligation, right or title to property is created,
acknowledged, transferred, increased, defeated, discharged or diminished, and
every right or interest therein.
The word "streets" includes alleys, lanes, courts, boulevards, public ways,
public squares, public places and sidewalks.
The word "owner" applied to a building or land shall include any part owner,
joint owner, tenant in common, joint tenant or lessee of the whole or of a part
of such building or land.
The word "tenant" or "occupant" applied to a building or land shall include any
person who occupies the whole or any part of such building or land whether
alone or with others.
Words prohibiting anything being done, except in accordance with a license or
permit or authority from a board or officer, shall be construed as giving such
board or officer power to license or permit or authorize such thing to be done.
The word "officer" shall include officers and boards in charge of departments
and members of such boards. Such reference as use of the word "City" shall mean
this Municipality. "Clerk," "Treasurer" or other officer titles used shall mean
City Clerk, City Treasurer of other City officer as the use may be applicable.
The term "wilfully" when applied to the intent with which an act is done or
omitted, implies simply a purpose or willingness to commit the act or make the
omission referred to. It does not require any intent to violate law, or to
injure another, or to acquire an advantage.
The term "neglect," "negligence," "negligent," and "negligently" imports a want
of such attention to the nature or probable consequences of the act or omission
as a prudent man ordinarily bestows in acting in his own concern.
The term "knowingly" imports only a knowledge that the facts exist which brings
the act or omission within the provisions of these ordinances. It does not
require any knowledge of the unlawfulness of such act or omission.
1-1-6: INTERPRETATIONS:
In the determination of the provisions of each Section of the Municipal Code
the following rules shall be observed:
   (A)   Intent to Defraud: Whenever an intent to defraud is required in order
to constitute an offense, it shall be sufficient if an intent appears to
defraud any person.
   (B)   Liability of Employers and Agents: When the provisions of any Section
of the Municipal Code prohibit the commission of an act, not only the person
actually doing the prohibited act or omitting the directed act, but also the
employer and all other persons concerned with or in aiding or abetting the said
person shall be guilty of the offense described and liable to the penalty set
forth.
1-1-7: PENALTIES:
In all cases where the same offense is made punishable or is created by
different clauses or sections of the official Municipal Code the prosecuting
officer may elect under which to proceed; but not more than one (1) recovery
shall be had against the same person for the same offense; provided, that the
revocation of a license or permit shall not be considered a recovery or penalty
so as to bar any other penalty being enforced.
Whenever the doing of any act or the omission to do any act constitutes a
breach of any Section or provision of the Municipal Code, and there shall be no
fine or penalty specifically declared for such breach, the provisions of the
general penalty clause shall apply and a separate offense shall be deemed
committed upon each day during or on which a breach or violation occurs or
continues.
1-1-8: LIABILITY OF OFFICERS:
No provision of the official Municipal Code designating the duties of any
officer or employee shall be so construed as to make such officer or employee
liable for any fine or penalty provided for a failure to perform such duty,
unless the intention of the Council to impose such fine or penalty on such
officer or employee is specifically and clearly expressed in the Section
creating the duty.
CHAPTER 2
SAVING CLAUSE
SECTION:
1-2-1: Repeal of General Ordinances
1-2-2: Public Utility Ordinances
1-2-3: Pending Suits
1-2-1: REPEAL OF GENERAL ORDINANCES:
All general ordinances of the City passed prior to the adoption of this Code
are hereby repealed, except such as are referred to herein as being still in
force or are by necessary implication herein reserved from repeal (subject to
the saving clauses contained in the following Section), from which are excluded
the following ordinances which are not hereby repealed; tax levy ordinances;
appropriation ordinances; ordinances relating to boundaries and annexations;
franchise ordinances and other ordinances granting special rights to persons or
corporations; contract ordinances and ordinances authorizing the execution of a
contract or the issuance of warrants; salary ordinances; ordinances
establishing, naming or vacating streets, alleys or other public places;
improvement ordinances; bond ordinances; ordinances relating to elections;
ordinances relating to the transfer or acceptance of real estate by or from the
City; and all special ordinances.
1-2-2: PUBLIC UTILITY ORDINANCES:
No ordinance relating to railroads or railroad crossings with streets and other
public ways, or relating to the conduct, duties, service or rates of public
utilities shall be repealed by virtue of the adoption of this Code or by virtue
of the preceding Section, excepting as this Code may contain provision for such
matters, in which case this Code shall be considered as amending such ordinance
or ordinances in respect of such provisions only.
1-2-3: PENDING SUITS:
No new ordinance shall be construed or held to repeal a former ordinance,
whether such former ordinance is expressly repealed or not, as to any offense
committed against such former ordinance or as to any act done, any penalty,
forfeiture or punishment so incurred, or any right accrued or claim arising
under the former ordinance, or in any way whatever to affect any such offense
or act so committed or so done, or any penalty, forfeiture or punishment so
incurred or any right accrued or claim arising before the new ordinance takes
effect, save only that the proceedings thereafter shall conform to the
ordinance in force at the time of such proceeding, so far as practicable. If
any penalty, forfeiture or punishment be mitigated by any provision of a new
ordinance, such provision may be, by the consent of the party affected, applied
to any judgment announced after the new ordinance takes effect.
This Section shall extend to all repeals, either by express words or
implication, whether the repeal is in the ordinance making any new provisions
upon the same subject or in any other ordinance.
Nothing contained in this or the preceding Section shall be construed as
abating any action now pending under or by virtue of any general ordinance of
the City herein repealed; or as discontinuing, abating, modifying or altering
any penalty accrued or to accrue, or as affecting the liability of any person,
firm or corporation, or as waiving any right of the City under any ordinance or
provision thereof in force at the time of adoption of this Code.
CHAPTER 3
PENALTY
SECTION:
1-3-1: Criminal Penalty
1-3-2: Application
1-3-3: Infractions
1-3-1: CRIMINAL PENALTY:
Any person convicted of a violation of any ordinance of the City for which a
criminal penalty is imposed, may be fined in a sum not to exceed one thousand
dollars ($1,000.00) for any offense and such person may be confined in the
Payette County Jail for a period of not more than six (6) months. Either or
both such fine and imprisonment may be imposed; and in addition thereto, any
person so convicted shall pay such costs as the court may assess. (Ord. 355, 1-
17-2017)
1-3-2: APPLICATION:
The penalty herein provided shall be applicable to every ordinance of the City
by which a person may be convicted of a crime which is designated as a
misdemeanor, the same as though it were a part of each and every separate
ordinance. Any person convicted of a violation of any ordinance of this City
for which a criminal penalty is imposed, shall be deemed guilty of a
misdemeanor. A separate offense shall be deemed committed for each day during
or on which a violation occurs or continues. (Ord. 355, 1-17-2017)
1-3-3: INFRACTIONS:
Any person who is convicted of an offense defined by either section 18-111 of
the Idaho Code or by any section of this Code as an infraction shall be guilty
of an infraction and shall be punished in accordance with section 18-113A of
the Idaho Code. (Ord. 355, 1-17-2017)
CHAPTER 4
DATUM PLANE
SECTION:
1-4-1: Official Base
1-4-2: Primal Bench Mark
1-4-3: Establishment of Elevations
1-4-1: OFFICIAL BASE:
The official City base or plane of reference for elevations in the City is
hereby fixed at a point ninety-nine and seventy-three one-hundredths feet
(99.73') below the top of the foundation of the Pioneer Block at the northeast
corner.
1-4-2: PRIMAL BENCH MARK:
The top of the bolt set in the concrete sidewalk at the northeast corner of the
City Hall is hereby declared to be the primal bench mark of the City and the
elevation thereof is one hundred feet (100') above City base.
1-4-3: ESTABLISHMENT OF ELEVATIONS:
All official elevations hereafter established in the City shall be described
with reference to their elevation as compared with the official base in feet
and decimal parts of a foot, no grade or official elevation shall be
established other than by ordinance and in the manner described in this
Chapter.
CHAPTER 5
ELECTIONS
SECTION:
1-5-1: Precinct
1-5-2: Hours Of Polling Places For City Elections
1-5-1: PRECINCT:
The city of New Plymouth is hereby declared one precinct, with one voting place
for city elections. (Ord. 85, 9-11-1967)
1-5-2: HOURS OF POLLING PLACES FOR CITY ELECTIONS:
The polls for all general and special city elections shall be open from eight
o'clock (8:00) A.M. Mountain time and will remain open until eight o'clock (8:
00) P.M. Mountain time. (Ord. 324, 10-5-2009)
CHAPTER 6
SALARIES
SECTION:
1-6-1: Salaries Of Elective Officers
1-6-2: Salaries Of Appointive Officers
1-6-1: SALARIES OF ELECTIVE OFFICERS:
The salaries of the elected officers of the city shall be as follows: (Ord. 92,
9-4-1969, eff. 1-1-1970)
 
Mayor              $175.00 per month
Councilmen (each)  125.00 per month
 
(Ord. 158, 8-18-1983, eff. 1-1-1984)
1-6-2: SALARIES OF APPOINTIVE OFFICERS:
The salaries of all appointed officers and employees of the city shall be as
established and approved by recorded action of the council. (1960 Code)
CHAPTER 7
MAYOR
SECTION:
1-7-1: Duties
1-7-2: Contract
1-7-3: Reward
1-7-4: Pardons
1-7-5: Veto Power
1-7-6: Accounts of Officers
1-7-7: Police Power
1-7-8: May Require Aid
1-7-9: Other Powers
1-7-1: DUTIES:
The Mayor, the superintending and administrative officer of the Municipality,
shall devote so much of his time to the duties of his office as an efficient
and faithful discharge thereof may require. He shall preside at all meetings of
the Council and shall have a vote when the Council is equally divided, and call
special meetings of the Council when necessary. He shall appoint all officers
and employees of the Municipality, subject to the approval of the Council, and
have such other powers as the Council may prescribe. He shall from time to time
provide for the Council such information and recommend such measures as he may
deem beneficial to the Municipality. He shall examine the grounds of all
complaints against any officer of the Municipality to determine existence of a
violation or neglect of duty and report to the Council the evidence thereof, if
deemed sufficient for the removal of said officer. He shall require that every
officer, on the expiration of his term of office or resignation or removal,
deliver to his successor all assets belonging to such office. He shall perform
all other duties required and necessary for the efficient operation of the
business of the Municipality.
1-7-2: CONTRACT:
The Mayor is authorized and empowered to sign his name officially for and in
behalf of the Municipality on all contracts, documents and papers to which the
Municipality is a party, and to require that the conditions in any instrument
are faithfully performed. He may borrow money on the credit of the Municipality
when so authorized by the Council.
1-7-3: REWARD:
The Mayor, whenever he deems it expedient, is hereby empowered to offer a
reward not exceeding one hundred dollars ($100.00) for the arrest and
conviction of any person charged with violating any of the provisions of this
Code.
1-7-4: PARDONS:
The Mayor is empowered to grant a pardon to any person imprisoned for a
violation of any of the provisions of this Code, and to remit so much of any
fine or forfeiture as in his judgment he may deem just and reasonable, and he
shall report such remittance or pardon to the Council at its next meeting.
1-7-5: VETO POWER:
The Mayor shall have power to veto or sign any ordinance passed by the Council
provided, that any ordinance vetoed by the Mayor may be passed over his veto by
a vote of two-thirds (2/3) of the members of the Council, and should the Mayor
neglect or refuse to sign any ordinance, the same shall become law without his
signature after the next regular meeting of the Council.
1-7-6: ACCOUNTS OF OFFICERS:
The Mayor shall have the power to require any officer of the Municipality to
exhibit his accounts or other papers and make reports to the Council in writing
on any subject or matter pertaining to the office.
1-7-7: POLICE POWER:
The Mayor shall have jurisdiction over all places within five (5) miles of the
Corporate Limits of the Municipality for the enforcement of any health or
quarantine ordinance and regulation and shall have jurisdiction in all matters,
excepting taxation, within one-half (1/2) mile of the Corporate Limits of the
Municipality.
1-7-8: MAY REQUIRE AID:
The Mayor is hereby authorized to call on every male inhabitant of the
Municipality over the age of eighteen (18) and under the age of fifty (50)
years to aid in enforcing the law.
1-7-9: OTHER POWERS:
The Mayor shall have all other powers provided by State Statute or by specific
provisions of this Code.
CHAPTER 8
THE COUNCIL
SECTION:
1-8-1: Duties
1-8-2: Ward Representation (Rep. by Ord. 196, 4-2-1990)
1-8-3: Vacancy; How Filled
1-8-4: How To Conduct Council Meeting
1-8-5: Elect President Of The Council
1-8-6: Time And Place Of Meeting
1-8-1: DUTIES:
Members of the Council, the legislative and policymaking branch of the
Municipality, shall devote so much of their time to the duties of their office
as an efficient and faithful discharge thereof may require. They shall attend
all meetings of the Council unless lawfully excused therefrom by the Mayor or
by a majority of the remaining members, and perform all duties which by the
nature of their office they should reasonably perform, such as the passing of
ordinances, resolutions and the investigation and study of work done for the
Municipality according to the committees upon which they may severally be
appointed by the Mayor. (1960 Code)
1-8-2: WARD REPRESENTATION:
(Rep. by Ord. 196, 4-2-1990)
1-8-3: VACANCY; HOW FILLED:
In the event an Office of Councilman shall become vacant, through death,
removal of residence, or for any other cause, the Mayor shall appoint, with the
approval of the Council, a resident of the ward to fill the unexpired portion
of the term to serve until the next general election, at which time the
unexpired term shall be filled by regular election. (1960 Code)
1-8-4: HOW TO CONDUCT COUNCIL MEETING:
There is hereby adopted for the purpose of establishing rules and regulations
for the conduct of Council meetings, the book entitled "How to Conduct a
Municipal Council Meeting" prepared by the Idaho Municipal League, three (3)
copies of which shall be on file in the Office of the Clerk, and the same is
hereby adopted and incorporated as fully as if set out at length herein. (1960
Code)
1-8-5: ELECT PRESIDENT OF THE COUNCIL:
At the time of taking office the Council shall elect one of its members
President of the Council who shall preside at all meetings of the Council and
perform all other duties of the Mayor in the absence of the Mayor; and, in the
absence of the President the Council shall elect one of their members to occupy
his place temporarily, who shall be styled acting President of the Council, and
the President and acting President, when occupying the place of Mayor, shall
have the same privileges as other members of the Council and all actions of the
President and acting President, while so acting, shall be binding upon the
Council and upon the Municipality as if performed by the Mayor. (1960 Code)
1-8-6: TIME AND PLACE OF MEETING:
Meetings shall be held at the City Hall on the first and third Mondays of each
month at six o'clock (6:00) P.M. (Ord. 385, 12-17-2018)
CHAPTER 9
APPOINTIVE OFFICERS
SECTION:
1-9-1: Appointments
1-9-2: Terms Of Office
1-9-3: Removal From Office
1-9-4: Bonds Of Officers
1-9-1: APPOINTMENTS:
The mayor shall appoint, subject to approval of the council, a clerk, attorney,
engineer and treasurer. The mayor may appoint, subject to approval by the
council, such other officers as may be deemed necessary for the efficient
operation of the business of the municipality. (Ord. 287, 7-7-2003)
1-9-2: TERMS OF OFFICE:
All appointments shall continue until resignation, retirement or removal of the
appointed official as set forth in section 1-9-3. (1960 Code; amd. Ord. 398,
10-21-2019)
1-9-3: REMOVAL FROM OFFICE:
Any appointed officer may be removed from office by the mayor with the
concurrence by and with the affirmative vote of one half (1/2) plus one (1) of
the members of the full council. The city council, by the unanimous vote of all
its members, may upon their own initiative remove any appointive officer. (1960
Code; amd. Ord. 398, 10-21-2019)
1-9-4: BONDS OF OFFICERS:
Certain officers shall give bonds in favor of the municipality with two (2) or
more sureties, or surety bonds may be furnished in lieu of personal bonds as
follows:
   Clerk      $10,000.00
   Treasurer   10,000.00
Bonds so furnished in accordance with the provisions of this chapter shall be
furnished at the expense of the municipality. (1960 Code)
CHAPTER 10
CLERK
SECTION:
1-10-1: Appointment And Removal
1-10-2: Duties
1-10-3: Records Of The Governing Body
1-10-4: Ordinances
1-10-5: Election Records
1-10-6: Notify Of Term Expirations
1-10-7: Official Seal
1-10-8: Copies Of Records
1-10-9: Collections To Treasurer
1-10-10: Licenses
1-10-11: Bonds
1-10-12: Warrants
1-10-13: Claims
1-10-14: Damages
1-10-1: APPOINTMENT AND REMOVAL:
   A.   The clerk shall be appointed by the mayor subject to the approval of a
majority vote of the council. The appointed clerk shall hold office until
removed by the mayor with the concurrence of the council. The vote of the
council on removal shall be by and with the affirmative vote of one half (1/2)
plus one (1) of the members of the full council.
   B.   The city council, by the unanimous vote of all its members, may upon
their own initiative remove the clerk. (Ord. 346, 9-21-2015; amd. Ord. 398, 10-
21-2019)
1-10-2: DUTIES:
In all cases where the duty is not expressly charged to any other department or
office the clerk shall have supervision, control and responsibility of all of
the records of the municipality. He shall serve as clerk of the governing body
and perform such other duties of a like nature as shall be required by that
body. (1960 Code)
1-10-3: RECORDS OF THE GOVERNING BODY:
The clerk shall be responsible for the recording, filing, indexing and
safekeeping of all proceedings of the governing body and shall have published
all proceedings, legal notices, ordinances and resolutions that are required to
be published by this code or by state statute. (1960 Code)
1-10-4: ORDINANCES:
The clerk shall record in full, uniformly and permanently, all ordinances and
he shall authenticate the same. (1960 Code)
1-10-5: ELECTION RECORDS:
The clerk shall keep and maintain all election records and have custody of all
property used in connection with elections. (1960 Code)
1-10-6: NOTIFY OF TERM EXPIRATIONS:
The clerk shall notify the appointing authority of the impending expiration of
the term of office of a member of any board or commission at least thirty (30)
days before the expiration of the term. (1960 Code)
1-10-7: OFFICIAL SEAL:
The clerk shall be the custodian of the official seal of the municipality.
(1960 Code)
1-10-8: COPIES OF RECORDS:
The clerk shall furnish to any member of the governing body a certified copy of
any record or document in his custody and he may furnish such a copy to any
other person upon payment of a fee to be determined by the governing body.
(1960 Code)
1-10-9: COLLECTIONS TO TREASURER:
Within ten (10) days after the first day of each month the clerk shall turn
over to the treasurer all funds collected by him during the preceding month.
(1960 Code)
1-10-10: LICENSES:
In all cases where the duty is not expressly charged to any other department or
office the clerk shall issue all licenses in accordance with the provisions of
this code. A record of all licenses issued, including the name of the person to
whom issued, the amount of the license fee, and the purpose of the license
shall be kept by the clerk. (1960 Code)
1-10-11: BONDS:
The clerk shall keep a complete record of all outstanding bonds of the
municipality and report such record regularly to the governing body. (1960
Code)
1-10-12: WARRANTS:
The clerk shall countersign all warrants and keep a "warrant register and
abstract of expenditures" showing the number and amount of warrants issued and
the person to whom issued, the date redeemed, the interest paid and the several
funds against which each of said warrants is drawn. (1960 Code)
1-10-13: CLAIMS:
All claims against the municipality must be filed in writing with the clerk.
Claims must present a full account of the items and must contain a verification
under oath by the claimant to the effect that the claim is correct, reasonable
and just and that no part of said claim has been paid. All such claims must be
approved by the governing body before payment can be made. (1960 Code)
1-10-14: DAMAGES:
All claims for damages against the municipality must be filed with the clerk
within six (6) months after such time as the damage is alleged to have accrued.
All such claims shall specify the time, place, character and cause of damage
and no action shall be maintained against the municipality for any claim for
damages until sixty (60) days have elapsed after such presentation. Allowance
of any claim for damages against the municipality shall be made only by
ordinance. (1960 Code)
CHAPTER 11
TREASURER
SECTION:
1-11-1: Appointment And Removal
1-11-2: Duties
1-11-3: Accounts
1-11-4: Monies
1-11-5: Collections
1-11-6: Warrants
1-11-7: Cancellation Of Warrants
1-11-8: Monthly Report
1-11-9: Quarterly Report
1-11-10: Delivery To Successor
1-11-1: APPOINTMENT AND REMOVAL:
   A.   The treasurer shall be appointed by the mayor subject to the approval
of a majority vote of the council. The appointed treasurer shall hold office
until removed by the mayor with the concurrence of the council. The vote of the
council on removal shall be by and with the affirmative vote of one half (1/2)
plus one (1) of the members of the full council.
   B.   The city council, by the unanimous vote of all its members, may upon
their own initiative remove the treasurer. (Ord. 346, 9-21-2015; amd. Ord. 398,
10-21-2019)
1-11-2: DUTIES:
In all cases where the duty is not expressly charged to any other department or
office the treasurer shall act to promote, secure and preserve the financial
and property interests of the municipality. He shall safely keep in designated
depositories all funds belonging to the municipality and all other securities
in safety deposit boxes of an approved institution designated by the governing
body. (1960 Code)
1-11-3: ACCOUNTS:
The treasurer shall keep in proper books a full and accurate account of all the
monies received and disbursed by him in behalf of the municipality, specifying
the time of receipt and disbursement, from whom received and to whom disbursed,
and on what account received and disbursed, and how paid. (1960 Code)
1-11-4: MONIES:
The treasurer shall receive and have custody of all monies paid to the
municipality and shall disburse monies upon the official warrant of the
municipality when so ordered by the governing body. (1960 Code)
1-11-5: COLLECTIONS:
The treasurer shall demand and receive all monies and fees owing to the
municipality whenever any person is indebted to the municipality in any manner,
and the means of collection of such debt is not otherwise provided for by law.
When any claim shall not be collectible by other methods he shall report the
same to the attorney for prosecution. (1960 Code)
1-11-6: WARRANTS:
Warrants shall be paid by the treasurer from funds available in the order in
which the warrants are presented for payment. When a warrant is presented for
payment and no funds are available the treasurer shall plainly mark the warrant
"Not Paid for Want of Funds" and enter the same in a book maintained for such
purpose which shall be known as the "warrant register". Such warrants shall
bear interest at the rate of seven percent (7%) per annum from the date of
presentation until paid.
Warrants shall be called for payment in the order in which they were presented
whenever sufficient funds are available to the treasurer to make such payment.
(1960 Code)
1-11-7: CANCELLATION OF WARRANTS:
The treasurer shall cancel all warrants and other evidence of debt against the
municipality, whenever paid by him, by writing or stamping across the face
thereof the words "Paid By The Treasurer" with the date of payment written or
stamped thereon. These warrants and evidences of debt, so canceled, shall be
delivered immediately to the clerk. (1960 Code)
1-11-8: MONTHLY REPORT:
The treasurer shall make a detailed report to the governing body during the
first week of each month showing the business of his office during the month
preceding, showing the balance on hand to the credit of the different funds,
the amounts received during the month, and on what account, together with such
other information as may be required by the governing body. (1960 Code)
1-11-9: QUARTERLY REPORT:
The treasurer shall cause to be published for at least one insertion in a
newspaper of general circulation in the municipality a full statement of the
receipts and expenditures of the municipality, showing sources of revenue and
disposition of funds. This quarterly report shall be published before the third
Monday of the months of May, August, November, and February. (1960 Code)
1-11-10: DELIVERY TO SUCCESSOR:
The treasurer shall deliver to his successor in office all materials, records,
and resources of the office. (1960 Code)
CHAPTER 12
ATTORNEY
SECTION:
1-12-1: Appointment
1-12-2: Suits And Actions
1-12-3: Judgments
1-12-4: Advice
1-12-5: Special Assessments
1-12-6: Ordinances And Documents
1-12-1: APPOINTMENT:
The attorney shall be appointed by the mayor subject to the approval of the
council. He shall hold office for the duration of his appointment unless sooner
removed by the mayor with the concurrence of the council. (1960 Code)
1-12-2: SUITS AND ACTIONS:
The attorney shall prosecute or defend any and all suits or actions at law or
equity to which the municipality may be a party, or in which it may be
interested, or which may be brought against, or by, any officer of the
municipality on behalf of the municipality, or in the capacity of such person
as an officer of the municipality. (1960 Code)
1-12-3: JUDGMENTS:
It shall be the duty of the attorney to see to the full enforcement of all
judgments or decrees rendered or entered in favor of the municipality and of
all similar interlocutory orders. (1960 Code)
1-12-4: ADVICE:
The attorney shall be the legal advisor of the municipality, and shall render
advice on all legal questions affecting the municipality, whenever requested to
do so by any municipal official. Upon request by the mayor or by the council,
he shall reduce any such opinion to writing. (1960 Code)
1-12-5: SPECIAL ASSESSMENTS:
It shall be the duty of the attorney to see to the completion of all special
assessment proceedings and condemnation proceedings. (1960 Code)
1-12-6: ORDINANCES AND DOCUMENTS:
It shall be the duty of the attorney to draft or supervise the phraseology of
any contract, lease or other documents or instruments, to which the
municipality may be a party; and upon request of the council to draft
ordinances covering any subjects within the power of the municipality. (1960
Code)

CHAPTER 22
INITIATIVE AND REFERENDUM
(Rep. by Ord. 359, 6-19-2017)
CHAPTER 23
INDUSTRIAL DEVELOPMENT CORPORATION
SECTION:
1-23-1: Creation; Powers
1-23-2: Powers And Duties
1-23-3: Charter
1-23-4: Board Of Directors
1-23-5: Conduct Of Corporate Affairs
1-23-6: Conflict Of Interest
1-23-7: Monies, Distribution And Earnings
1-23-1: CREATION; POWERS:
   (A)   The City does hereby create and with this chapter does create a public
corporation to carry out the purposes of the Act. This chapter will not be
construed to limit or restrict the purposes of the Act, but shall be liberally
construed to affect such purposes.
   (B)   The name of the public corporation shall be the New Plymouth
Industrial Development Corporation (the "corporation"). (Ord. 157, 6-6-1983)
1-23-2: POWERS AND DUTIES:
   (A)   The corporation shall have all the powers and authority set forth in
the Act and shall be subject to all the limitations and conditions therein
contained. Said powers and limitations are set forth in the charter, a copy of
which is attached hereto and incorporated herein by reference thereto, as if
set forth in full verbatim; and said enumerations shall not be construed as a
limitation upon the powers of the corporation.
   (B)   The Corporation shall have all the powers granted by the Act. Such
powers shall include, without limitation, all powers set forth in the charter,
together with any express or implied powers contained within title 50, section
27, Idaho Code, which are not expressly set forth in said charter.
1-23-3: CHARTER:
The Corporation charter (the "charter") is hereby created and issued by the
City to the Corporation. Said charter grants to the Corporation all powers
authorized by the Act and subjects the same to all the limitations imposed
thereby. The charter is hereby approved, pursuant to section 50-2703.1 of the
Act. The charter may be amended, altered or changed at any time at the
discretion of the City and the City may terminate the public corporation if
contracts entered into are not impaired. With this Chapter, however, the City
does not attempt to delegate any of its attributes of sovereignty to the public
corporation. The existence of the corporation commences simultaneously when
this Chapter becomes effective.
1-23-4: BOARD OF DIRECTORS:
The Board of Directors to the Corporation (the "Board") shall be comprised of
three (3) residents of the City, appointed by the Mayor and confirmed by the
City Council. Of the members first appointed, one member shall serve for a one
year term, one for a two (2) year term and one for a three (3) year term.
Thereafter, upon the expiration of a term of appointment, each member shall be
appointed to a three (3) year term. If a vacancy occurs during an unexpired
term, the Mayor, with the confirmation of the Council, shall appoint a member,
who shall also be a resident of the City, to serve the remainder of the
unexpired term. A simple majority of the members of the Board shall constitute
a quorum and the approval of the majority of a quorum shall be sufficient and
necessary for the Board to take any action.
1-23-5: CONDUCT OF CORPORATE AFFAIRS:
The affairs of the Corporation shall be conducted and carried out by the Board.
The Board shall elect officers from its own members and shall consist of a
president, vice-president and a secretary-treasurer. These officers shall be
elected at the initial meeting of the Board in each calendar year and shall
serve until their successors have been duly elected. The Board may elect other
such officers as it shall, from time to time, determine to be necessary or
desirable and may appoint agents or employees as the Board determines the same
shall be required. The Board shall adopt by-laws governing the election of
officers, the power and duty of the officers, the filling of vacancies in
offices, scheduling and giving of notice, the conduct of the meetings and the
conduct of the Corporation. Such by-laws, rules and regulations may be amended
from time to time by the Board, provided that such amendments shall be
consistent with the provisions herein contained. Members of the Board shall
serve without compensation, but may be reimbursed for expenses as may be
provided in the by-laws, rules and regulations of the Board, with the approval
of the City.
1-23-6: CONFLICT OF INTEREST:
No director, officer, agent, employee or official of the Corporation shall have
a direct or indirect financial interest in any property to be included in or
any contract for property, service or materials to be furnished or used in
connection with any industrial development facility financed through the
Corporation.
1-23-7: MONIES, DISTRIBUTION AND EARNINGS:
   (A)   The City may not give or lend any money or property in aid of the
Corporation except as expressly authorized by the Act. This provision shall not
preclude the City from dealing with the Corporation on an arms length basis.
   (B)   Any net earnings of the Corporation beyond those necessary for
retirement of indebtedness incurred by it shall inure to the benefit of the
City and not for the benefit of any other person or entity. Said Corporation
shall be subject to annual audits and the City shall audit said Corporation
annually and additionally from time to time as the City may so desire.
   (C)   All expenses incurred by the Corporation shall be repaid from the
proceeds of any issued revenue bonds or from money or property paid by a user
or other private source. The funds and property of the City shall not be
responsible for repayment of any expenses of said Corporation. The Corporation
shall not co-mingle the proceeds of one bond issue with the proceeds of another
bond issue or with the monies of any other public corporation, municipality,
person or entity.
   (D)   Upon the dissolution of the Corporation, title to any and all property
owned by the Corporation shall vest in the City. (Ord. 157, 6-6-83)
CHAPTER 24
CONFIDENTIAL INFORMATION
SECTION:
1-24-1: Employee Files
1-24-2: Law Enforcement Information
1-24-1: EMPLOYEE FILES:
   (A)   Files Are Confidential: All documents, memoranda or other information
which is included, or intended to be included, in an employee's file is
confidential.
   (B)   Authorized Disclosures: No information which is included in an
employee's file shall be disclosed except in the manner and form following:
      1.   Confidential information contained within an employee's file may be
used by that employee's supervisor or the City Council for job evaluation and
other legitimate reasons connected to the employee's job performance.
      2.   Confidential information may be disclosed to third parties only upon
written consent of the employee, or if the employee has requested another party
to seek the information for job related purposes.
      3.   Nothing herein shall be intended to preclude the use of any
confidential information by any appointed City officials or City advisors when
needed for purposes of litigation, evaluating claims or evaluating potential
litigation.
   (C)   Violations: Any disclosures in violation of this Section shall be
deemed a misdemeanor. (Ord. 178, 4-6-87)
1-24-2: LAW ENFORCEMENT INFORMATION:
   (A)   Information Confidential: Information collected by any law enforcement
agency during the course of an investigation concerning a matter occurring in
the City is confidential.
   (B)   Authorized Disclosures:
      1.   No information so collected shall be disclosed to any outside
source, other than to other law enforcement agencies, the prosecuting attorney
and the appointed prosecuting attorney for legitimate law enforcement reasons.
      2.   Any information collected herein shall be made available to the City
Council or its agents or appointees at any time, for any reason. Such
information, however, shall not be made public nor disclosed, except for
legitimate law enforcement reasons or upon proper authorization obtained
through court orders during related discovery.
   (C)   Violations: Any disclosures in violation of this Section shall be
deemed a misdemeanor. (Ord. 179, 4-6-87)
CHAPTER 25
OFFICIAL COMPREHENSIVE PLAN
SECTION:
1-25-1: Adoption Of Plan
1-25-1: ADOPTION OF PLAN:
Ordinance 216, dated October 17, 1994, being the City's Official Comprehensive
Plan, and any amendments thereto, are hereby incorporated herein and made a
part hereof by reference. Said Comprehensive Plan is on file in the office of
the City Clerk. (Ord. 216, 10-17-1994)
TITLE II
COMMISSIONS AND BOARDS
CHAPTER 1
PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION 1
(Rep. by Ord. 363, 9-5-2017)
 
Notes
1 1. See title XI, chapter 3 of this Code.
CHAPTER 2
BOARD OF HEALTH
SECTION:
2-2-1: Board of Health Created; Personnel
2-2-2: Appointment of Board; Term of Office
2-2-3: Powers of Board
2-2-4: Mayor Chairman of Board
2-2-5: Quorum
2-2-1: BOARD OF HEALTH CREATED; PERSONNEL:
A Board of Health for the City is hereby created to consist of the following
members:
The Mayor, one other member of the City Council and one other citizen of the
City. Provided that one member of said Board of Health shall be a regularly
licensed and practicing physician within the City.
2-2-2: APPOINTMENT OF BOARD; TERM OF OFFICE:
The members of the Board of Health shall be appointed by the Mayor with
approval of the City Council of said City and shall hold their office until
their successors are appointed and qualify.
2-2-3: POWERS OF BOARD:
The Board of Health, or any member or members delegated therefrom, shall have
power to examine private premises, as well as public, in the interest of the
health of the City, and, if deemed necessary by said Board, to cause any and
all premises, buildings, or other place or places, to be cleaned or
disinfected, or both; and to adopt and enforce rules and regulations of a
sanitary character that may be deemed necessary. They shall have such power and
authority as is delegated by the laws of the State of Idaho to the Boards of
Health of like degree.
2-2-4: MAYOR CHAIRMAN OF BOARD:
The Mayor shall be Chairman of the Board of Health and shall have power to call
the Board together at any and all times and in case of his absence, inability
or refusal so to act, then the other members may call and hold meetings.
Provided that the minutes of such meeting shall show the absence, inability or
refusal of the Chairman to call such meeting.
2-2-5: QUORUM:
A majority of said Board shall constitute a quorum for the transaction of any
and all business of said Board.
CHAPTER 3
LIBRARY BOARD
SECTION:
2-3-1: Appointment; Term of Office
2-3-2: Organization and Powers
2-3-3: Tax Levy
2-3-4: Creation of Library Board
2-3-5: For Use by Residents and Nonresidents
2-3-6: Reservation of Authority
2-3-7: Effective Date of Users' Cards
2-3-8: Damaging Library Property
2-3-9: Implied Agreement
2-3-10: Retention of Property
2-3-11: Limitation of Number of Books
2-3-12: Family Issues of Cards
2-3-13: Penalty
2-3-1: APPOINTMENT; TERM OF OFFICE:
The Mayor, with the consent of the Council, may appoint a Library Board
consisting of five (5) members, one of which shall be a member of the Council.
Such Directors shall hold their office for three (3) years from the date of
appointment, and until their successors are appointed, but upon their first
appointment they shall divide themselves at their first meeting by lot, into
three (3) classes; two (2) members shall form the first class and shall serve
for one year; two (2) members shall form the second class and shall serve for
two (2) years; and one member shall form the third class and shall serve for
three (3) years. No compensation shall be paid or allowed to any member of the
Library Board in any manner whatsoever.
2-3-2: ORGANIZATION AND POWERS:
Said Board shall, immediately after their appointment, meet and organize by
electing one of their number president, and by the election of such other
officers as they may deem necessary. They shall make and adopt such rules and
regulations as may be expedient. They shall have exclusive control of the
expenditure of all moneys collected and the supervision, care and custody of
all buildings. They may appoint a librarian and assistants and prescribe rules
for their conduct. (1960 Code)
2-3-3: TAX LEVY:
Pursuant to section 33-2602 of the Idaho Code, the City Council shall annually
levy and cause to be collected as other taxes are, a tax not exceeding five (5)
mills on the dollar of the taxable property of the City to constitute a Library
Fund, which shall be kept by the Treasurer, separate and apart from other
moneys of the City, which shall be used exclusively for the purchase of books,
periodicals, necessary furniture and fixtures and whatever is required for the
maintenance of such library.
2-3-4: CREATION OF LIBRARY BOARD:
The City Council hereby creates and establishes a Library Board, which Board is
hereby authorized to perform all acts allowed by Statute. By the establishment
of this Board, the Council does not relinquish or surrender any rights or
authority to act itself as the Library Board, but reserves the right to act
concurrently with or separately from said Board. From time to time in the
following sections of this Chapter, the Council may reserve specific authority,
but such reservations shall not be construed as a limitation on the general
reservation herein stated.
2-3-5: FOR USE BY RESIDENTS AND NONRESIDENTS:
The library established under this Chapter shall be forever free for the use of
the residents of the City, subject to such reasonable rules and regulations as
the Library Board or the City Council may find necessary to adopt and publish
in order to render the use of the library for the greatest benefit to the
greatest number of persons, and by rule or ordinance the Board or City Council
may exclude and cut off from the use of said library any and all persons who
shall wilfully violate such rules and regulations. Said Council reserves the
right, from time to time, to set fees to be charged to nonresidents. A
nonresident shall be defined as any person who does not live within the
corporate City limits.
2-3-6: RESERVATION OF AUTHORITY:
The City Council hereby reserves for itself the authority and power to set
fees, establish fines and penalties, and the authority to impose such rules and
regulations as the said Council deems fit in addition to, or concurrently with,
the rules and regulations set by the Library Board.
2-3-7: EFFECTIVE DATE OF USERS' CARDS:
The City Council further reserves the right to set rules controlling the
effective and expiration dates of cards which are issued to library users.
2-3-8: DAMAGING LIBRARY PROPERTY:
It shall be unlawful for any person to wilfully or intentionally cut, tear,
deface, break, injure or destroy any book, map, chart or any other property
belonging to the public library.
2-3-9: IMPLIED AGREEMENT:
Every person who takes a book or removes an article belonging to the public
library, agrees that the book or article is in good condition, has been
examined by the person removing the same, and that they will return the book or
property in as good condition as when the book or item was removed from the
library, reasonable wear and tear accepted.
2-3-10: RETENTION OF PROPERTY:
No person shall wilfully retain any property belonging to the public library
for more than thirty (30) days after the same has been removed from the
library. Any person who removes any book or article from the library impliedly
consents upon making application for a library card or when checking out a book
or an article that the book or article shall be returned within thirty (30)
days from the date it is checked out or removed from said library.
2-3-11: LIMITATION OF NUMBER OF BOOKS:
The City Council specifically reserves the right to limit by regulation or
rule, the number of books that an individual or family can remove from the
library at any given time. Such a regulation or rule shall have the same force
and effect as the implementing ordinance would have if the limitations were set
out herein.
2-3-12: FAMILY ISSUES OF CARDS:
All cards issued out of the library provided for by City Code shall be deemed
family cards and shall be deemed issued only to responsible persons over
eighteen (18) years of age or to the heads of households. No card shall be
issued to a minor child except in the event that a responsible adult agrees to
accept full liability and responsibility for the actions of the child receiving
the card. Any adult to whom the card is issued, or who signs a consent allowing
a card to be issued to a minor child, shall be financially responsible for any
loss or damage to any book or article removed from the library, or any damage
done to any article within the library, or for any overdue books.
2-3-13: PENALTY:
   (A)   Any person who shall wilfully violate this Chapter by intentionally
cutting, tearing, defacing, breaking, injuring or destroying any property
belonging to the public library, whether within the premises or after the
property has been removed from the premises, shall be deemed guilty of a
misdemeanor and shall be punished by a maximum fine not exceeding three hundred
dollars ($300.00), or by imprisonment not to exceed six (6) months in the
Payette County jail or by both imprisonment and fine.
   (B)   Any person who retains in his possession any article belonging to the
public library for a period of more than thirty (30) days after removing the
same from said library, shall be responsible to the library for the full
replacement value of the article or item, together with any court costs or
attorney's fees required or any other costs incurred in locating the parties
and securing payment.
   (C)   Any person who shall unintentionally or accidentally cut, tear, break,
injure or destroy any property belonging to the public library, shall be
responsible for the full replacement value of the item together with any
attorney's fees and court costs required in securing payment of the same.
   (D)   Any person who violates any section of this Chapter shall be subject
to having his library card revoked immediately without notice of any kind.
(Ord. 134, 7-2-79, eff. 7-12-79)
CHAPTER 4
DEVELOPMENT IMPACT FEE ADVISORY COMMITTEES
SECTION:
2-4-1: Development Impact Fee Advisory Committees
2-4-2: Committee Membership
2-4-3: Committees Charge
2-4-4: Advisory Committee Organization
2-4-5: Committee Reporting
2-4-6: Review Of Committee’s Reports And Recommendations
2-4-1: DEVELOPMENT IMPACT FEE ADVISORY COMMITTEES:
The following named development impact fee advisory committees of City of New
Plymouth (“City”) are established as standing permanent committees:
   A.   City of New Plymouth Development Impact Fee Advisory Committee; and
   B.   New Plymouth Fire Protection District Development Impact Fee Advisory
Committee by an intergovernmental agreement.
(Ord. 424, 9-5-2023)
2-4-2: COMMITTEE MEMBERSHIP:
The members of the City of New Plymouth Development Impact Fee Advisory
Committee shall be appointed (including vacancy appointments) by mayor with the
advice and consent of the city council. The members of the development impact
fee advisory committees established by an intergovernmental agreement shall be
appointed as provided in the intergovernmental agreement (including vacancy
appointments) for a term stated of at least one (1) year.
   A.   Notice of Committee Appointments: Pursuant to the intergovernmental
agreements, notice of appointments shall be provided to the city clerk and the
city council within seven (7) days of any such appointment.
   B.   Committee Membership Requirements: There shall be no fewer than five
(5) members on the development impact fee advisory committees (“advisory
committees”) and two (2) or more members must be active in the business of
development, building, or real estate. All members must reside within the
service area of the applicable capital improvement plan. No members shall be
employees or officials of the city or of the district whose service area is the
subject of the applicable capital improvements plan, with which the city has an
intergovernmental agreement to enact an impact fee ordinance.
(Ord. 424, 9-5-2023)
2-4-3: COMMITTEES CHARGE:
Each development impact fee advisory committee established by this chapter
shall serve as an advisory committee to the city council. In the case of
advisory committees established by an intergovernmental agreement, the advisory
committees shall also serve as an advisory committee to the governing body of
any district with whom the city has an intergovernmental agreement to enact an
impact fee ordinance. Each advisory committee is charged with the following
responsibilities:
   A.   Assist in adopting land use assumptions;
   B.   Review the capital improvements plan;
   C.   Monitor and evaluate implementation of the capital improvements plan;
   D.   File with the impact fee administrator and the city clerk (at least
annually) a report of any perceived inequities in implementing the capital
improvements plan or imposing development impact fees;
   E.   Advise the city council and the governing body of the other party (per
the respective intergovernmental agreement) of the need to update or revise
land use assumptions of capital improvements plans;
   F.   The city and the governing body of the other party (per the respective
intergovernmental agreement) shall make available to the advisory committees,
upon request, all financial and accounting information, professional reports in
relation to development and implementation of land use assumptions of the
capital improvements plans, and of the need for periodic updates to the capital
improvements plan(s).
(Ord. 424, 9-5-2023)
2-4-4: ADVISORY COMMITTEE ORGANIZATION:
The impact fee administrator shall staff the advisory committee in order to
provide the committee with needed information for the committee’s review and
for the committee’s compliance with the Open Meeting Law (Chapter 2 of Title 74
Idaho Code).
   A.   The advisory committee shall select its officers, which include a
chairman, vice chairman and a secretary of the committee;
   B.   The chairman shall conduct the meetings of the committee. The duties of
the chairman shall be performed by the vice chairman in the absence of the
chairman or as delegated by the chairman. The chairman and the vice chairman
shall be members of the committee;
   C.   The impact fee administrator shall serve as the secretary of the
committee and shall take minutes and post agenda notices as required by the
Open Meeting Law. The secretary is not a member of the committee;
   D.   The committee shall establish a regular meeting schedule;
   E.   The agenda of each meeting shall include the approval of the minutes of
the last meeting and the secretary shall provide a copy of the approved minutes
to the city council and to the respective governing body of the party with whom
the city has an intergovernmental agreement;
   F.   Fifty (50) percent of the membership of the committee shall constitute
a quorum. Once a quorum is established for a meeting, the subsequent absence of
a member present for creating the quorum shall not dismiss the quorum; and
   G.   A majority vote of those present at any meeting is sufficient to carry
motions.
(Ord. 424, 9-5-2023)
2-4-5: COMMITTEE REPORTING:
The advisory committees report directly to the city council and to the
respective governing body of the party with whom the city has an
intergovernmental agreement.
(Ord. 424, 9-5-2023)
2-4-6: REVIEW OF COMMITTEE’S REPORTS AND RECOMMENDATIONS:
The city council and the respective governing body of any district with whom
the city has an intergovernmental agreement shall each consider the advisory
committee’s recommended revision(s) to the capital improvements plan (as
relevant) at least once every twelve (12) months. Each advisory committee shall
make recommendations intended to ensure that the development impact fees are
equitable, so that the impact fee charged to a development do not exceed a
proportionate share of system improvements costs, and that the procedures for
administering impact fees remain efficient.
(Ord. 424, 9-5-2023)
TITLE III
DEPARTMENTS
CHAPTER 1
POLICE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
3-1-1: Department Created
3-1-2: Duties
3-1-3: Witness Fee
3-1-4: Rules And Regulations
3-1-5: Matron
3-1-6: Rewards
3-1-7: Minimum Service Requirements
3-1-1: DEPARTMENT CREATED:
There is hereby created a Police Department which shall consist of the Chief of
Police and such other personnel as may be provided by the Governing Body of the
Municipality. (1960 Code)
3-1-2: DUTIES:
It shall be the duty of the members of the Police Department to see to the
enforcement of all of the laws of the Municipality and all statutes applicable
therein; and to preserve order and prevent infractions of the law and arrest
violators thereof. (1960 Code)
3-1-3: WITNESS FEE:
Every member of the Police Department shall appear as a witness whenever
necessary in a prosecution for a violation of any law or of any State or
Federal law. No such member shall retain any witness fee for service as witness
in any action or suit to which the Municipality is a party; any fees paid for
such services shall be turned over to the Chief of Police, who shall deposit
the same with the Treasurer. (1960 Code)
3-1-4: RULES AND REGULATIONS:
The Chief of the Police Department may make or prescribe such rules and
regulations as he shall deem advisable; such rules, when approved by the
Governing Body, shall be binding on such members. Such rules and regulations
may cover, besides the conduct of the members, uniforms and equipment to be
worn or carried, hours of service, vacations and all other similar matters
necessary or desirable for the better efficiency of the Department. (1960 Code)
3-1-5: MATRON:
The Mayor, with the consent of the Council, may appoint a Police Matron, who
shall perform such duties as may be assigned to her by the Chief of Police or
by the Mayor. (1960 Code)
3-1-6: REWARDS:
The Chief of Police, for meritorious service rendered by any member of the
police force in the due discharge of his duty, may permit such member to retain
for his own benefit, so far as he may be permitted by law, any reward or
present tendered him therefor, and it shall be cause of removal for any member
of the force to receive any such reward or present without notice thereof to
the Chief of Police and without his permission. (1960 Code)
3-1-7: MINIMUM SERVICE REQUIREMENTS:
Before a City police officer is sent to the Police Officers Standards and
Training Academy (POST) for certification, that officer shall be required to
sign an agreement that after graduation the officer shall remain with the City
for a minimum of one year. If during that one-year period following graduation,
the officer voluntarily quits or voluntarily separates from the City, that
officer shall reimburse the City for any and all costs which are incurred by
the City, which costs are associated with that officer's attendance at POST.
Those costs may include, but are not limited to, wages paid for shift coverage
in the officer's absence. (Ord. 227, 5-6-1996)
CHAPTER 2
FIRE DEPARTMENT
(Rep. by Ord. 362, 8-23-2017)
CHAPTER 3
WATER DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
3-3-1: Water System Property Of City
3-3-2: Water Superintendent In Charge Of System; Duties
3-3-3: Turning Water On
3-3-4: Application
3-3-5: Plumbing
3-3-6: Meters
3-3-7: Reading Meters
3-3-8: Rates Established By Resolution - No New Connections Outside City
3-3-9: Monthly Statement; Nonpayment
3-3-10: Responsibility For Accounts And Write Offs
3-3-11: Water User's Fee
3-3-12: Separate Meter Requirement
3-3-13: Fire Hydrants
3-3-1: WATER SYSTEM PROPERTY OF CITY:
All mains, laterals, pipes, hydrants and fixtures now laid, constructed or
installed, or hereafter to be laid, constructed or installed in, under, across
or through the streets, avenues, alleys and other thoroughfares of the City, or
adjacent territory, for supplying water to said City and the inhabitants
thereof, are hereby declared to be the property of the City, under the control
thereof and subject to the provisions of this chapter. (Ord. 76, 5-4-1964)
3-3-2: WATER SUPERINTENDENT IN CHARGE OF SYSTEM; DUTIES:
The Water Superintendent shall have general supervision over the waterworks of
the City, and appurtenances thereto, under the direction of the Mayor and
Council. Said Superintendent shall attend to the tapping of mains, and laying
and connecting laterals and installation of meters and meter boxes, and shall
see that all open ditches and excavations on or along the streets, alleys and
thoroughfares of said City are carefully guarded by rails and lights or other
proper warning signals. He shall have charge of and operate the pumping
stations and reservoirs and shall keep the mains of said system filled with
pure and wholesome water at a pressure sufficient for proper fire protection.
Said Superintendent shall also keep an inventory of all property belonging to
the water system and shall, with the consent of the Mayor and Council, purchase
supplies and equipment necessary for the maintenance of the system. He shall,
upon request, attend meetings of the Council and render such reports and
statements as may be required. He shall perform such other duties as may be
required of him by law or order of the Mayor or Council, and to the end that
the provisions of this section may be carried out, said Superintendent shall be
allowed such assistance as the Mayor or Council may deem necessary and proper.
(Ord. 209, 6-7-1993)
3-3-3: TURNING WATER ON:
   (A)   No water from the City water supply shall be turned on for service
into any premises by any person other than the Superintendent or some person
authorized by him to perform this service. (Ord. 234, 12-16-1996)
   (B)   No water shall be turned on until there is first paid to the City
Clerk a deposit of one hundred thirty five dollars ($135.00). A deposit shall
not be refunded until the depositor has made twelve (12) consecutive timely
payments. (Ord. 369, 12-4-2017)
3-3-4: APPLICATION:
Application to have water turned on shall be made in writing to the Clerk, and
shall contain an agreement by the applicant to abide by and accept all of the
provisions of this chapter as conditions governing the use of the City water
supply by the applicant. (Ord. 76, 5-4-1964)
3-3-5: PLUMBING:
No water shall be turned on for service in premises in which the plumbing does
not comply with the specifications of the City; provided that water may be
turned on for construction work in unfinished buildings, subject to the
provisions of this chapter. (Ord. 76, 5-4-1964)
3-3-6: METERS:
All premises using City water must be equipped with an adequate water meter
which will be furnished by the City upon payment of those installation charges
established by resolution by the New Plymouth City Council.
All meters shall be installed under the direction of the Superintendent and
subject to his approval. The Superintendent shall have access to any building
at any reasonable hour for the purpose of inspection of any part of the water
system. (Ord. 364, 9-18-2017)
3-3-7: READING METERS:
The Superintendent shall read or cause to be read every water meter used in the
City at such times as are necessary so that the bills may be sent out at the
proper time. (Ord. 209, 6-7-1993)
3-3-8: RATES ESTABLISHED BY RESOLUTION - NO NEW CONNECTIONS OUTSIDE CITY:
   (A)   All minimum monthly charges for water and sewer, all bond redemption
fees for sewer and water and all other water and sewer charges, shall be set by
a resolution of the New Plymouth City Council and shall be paid in accordance
with the terms of the resolution.
   (B)   Water and sewer fees shall not apply to vacant or abandoned lots which
do not have or have not had an existing water meter.
   (C)   Connections to City water shall not be made to property or buildings
erected on property outside the City limits. (Ord. 364, 9-18-2017)
3-3-9: MONTHLY STATEMENT; NONPAYMENT:
   (A)   Monthly statements for water used shall be dated and sent out at such
times as specified by the Mayor and Council. (Ord. 209, 6-7-1993)
   (B)   Bills for water, sewer and garbage shall be due and payable within ten
(10) days of mailing. Any bill not paid by the twenty fifth of the month shall
be delinquent. Any bill that becomes delinquent shall incur an automatic
fifteen dollar ($15.00) delinquency charge. In the event the past due amount
and delinquency fee is not paid by the fifteenth day of the following month,
the water service shall be terminated forthwith.
   (C)   If the water supply to any building, dwelling, residence, or any place
where water supplied by the City is used, has been shut off because of
nonpayment, the water supply shall not be restored until all amounts which are
due and owing for previously provided water services together with any current
charges have been paid and a reconnection fee of twenty five dollars ($25.00)
has been paid to the City. (Ord. 364, 9-18-2017)
   (D)   After any water supply has been disconnected for nonpayment, no
person, except the City Public Works Superintendent or a person duly authorized
by him, shall reconnect said water supply. Any person who reconnects any water
supply after the same has been disconnected shall be guilty of a misdemeanor
and punished by the laws of the State. Should any unauthorized person reconnect
any water supply, in violation of this chapter, the City shall have the right
to immediately and without notice remove the water meter to any building,
structure or premises supplied thereby. (Ord. 209, 6-7-1993)
3-3-10: RESPONSIBILITY FOR ACCOUNTS AND WRITE OFFS:
   (A)   Owner Liable: The owner of each building connected to the water and
sewer system shall be deemed primarily liable for the payment of water and
sewer billings. Pursuant to arrangements with the owner, a tenant may pay such
charges and reduce the owner's liability by the amount of any such payment.
Acceptance by the City of such payment from a tenant shall not constitute a
waiver by the City of the owner's primary liability for charges not paid by the
tenant. Any arrangements made between the tenant and the owner shall have no
effect on the City and the City shall not incur any liability to the owner for
not disconnecting the water service in the event of nonpayment by the tenant.
   (B)   Billing Address: It shall be the responsibility of the owner to keep
the City informed as to an address where the water and sewer billing should be
sent in the event of nonpayment by the tenant. (Ord. 181, 6-15-1987; amd. Ord.
353, 11-7-2016)
   (C)   Write Off Accounts: Writing off a delinquent account shall not act as
a forgiveness of the underlying obligation. Notwithstanding any other section
of this Code nor any other remedy permitted by State Statute or City ordinance,
in the event a water or sewer user fails to pay a water or sewer bill and
allows the bill to become delinquent, in addition to any other remedies
provided by law, the City shall have the following remedies: 1) the City may
turn the account over to a collection agency for collection; 2) the City may
attach the unpaid obligation to a different water or sewer account in the
ratepayer's name, whether the account is in existence or subsequently created
and continue to bill the original account; 3) refuse to offer new water or
sewer services to the ratepayer until the account is paid in full. (Ord. 353,
11-7-2016)
3-3-11: WATER USER'S FEE:
   (A)   There shall be and this does establish a user's fee to be set by
resolution for single-family dwellings, multi-family dwellings and for
commercial and industrial hookups. That charge shall be added to every water
bill of all persons receiving water services from the City.
   (B)   The purpose of the user's fee shall be to purchase materials,
including, but not limited to, pipes, valves and other material which may be
necessary or convenient for the improvement or replacement of portions of the
presently existing water system. Such cost shall include labor and installation
as replacement or repair may be needed.
   (C)   The monies collected from the user's fee shall be accounted for
separately and funds from that account may be used only for the specific
purpose set forth herein, unless additional funds may be obtained through
private, State or governmental grants for the improvement of the City water
system. (Ord. 364, 9-18-2017)
3-3-12: SEPARATE METER REQUIREMENT:
Every residential or commercial unit or portion thereof for which there is
generated a billing for a water user therein, shall be served by its own water
meter. Each unit shall then be billed separately for its individual water
usage. In the event a property owner chooses not to install a water meter to
meet the requirements of this section, then the property owner shall be
responsible for payment of the water billing. (Ord. 258, 10-18-1999)
3-3-13: FIRE HYDRANTS:
   (A)   It is unlawful to open, operate, activate or draw water from a fire
hydrant belonging to the City unless the fire hydrant is being operated by a
fire crew suppressing a fire or a fire crew in training or unless the person
operating the fire hydrant has first received written permission from the
Public Works Superintendent of the City of New Plymouth.
   (B)   Water drawn from a fire hydrant or bulk water dispenser shall be
metered and charged for as follows:
 
Resident/agriculture use $ 2.00/1,000 gallons
Resident/commercial use  5.00/1,000 gallons
Any other use            10.00/1,000 gallons
 
   (C)   Any person who violates this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor
and punished in accordance with the misdemeanor laws of the State of Idaho.
(Ord. 334, 6-20-2011)
TITLE IV
BUILDING REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
BUILDING CODE
SECTION:
4-1-1: Adoption Of Codes
4-1-2: Building Permits
4-1-3: Permit Fees
4-1-4: Penalty
4-1-1: ADOPTION OF CODES:
The following codes as adopted by the State of Idaho are adopted as the
official Building Codes of the City of New Plymouth, Idaho:
   (A)   International Building Code: The International Building Code, 2018
edition, prepared by the International Code Council, Inc., as adopted by the
State of Idaho or the Idaho Building Code Board, together with any amendments
or revisions to the International Building Code made by the Idaho Building Code
Board through the negotiated rulemaking process;
   (B)   Idaho Residential Code: The Idaho Residential Code, 2018 edition,
prepared by the International Code Council, Inc., as adopted by the State of
Idaho or the Idaho Building Code Board, and amended by the Idaho Building Code
Board through the negotiated rulemaking process;
   (C)   International Energy Conservation Code: The International Energy
Conservation Code, 2018 edition, prepared by the International Code Council,
Inc., together with any amendments or revisions to the International Energy
Conservation Code made by the Idaho Building Code Board through the negotiated
rulemaking process;
   (D)   International Mechanical Code: The 2018 version of the International
Mechanical Code;
   (E)   International Fire Code: The 2015 version of the International Fire
Code;
   (F)   Manufactured Home Installation Standards: The current version of the
State of Idaho, Division of Building Safety, manufactured home installation
standards, together with appendices thereto;
   (G)   Public Works Construction: The current version of the "Idaho Standards
for Public Works Construction", together with any amendments, changes,
modifications, appendices or successor codes thereto;
   (H)   National Electrical Code: The latest edition of the National
Electrical Code as adopted by the state of Idaho; and
   (I)   International Plumbing Code: The 2018 International Plumbing Code as
adopted by the state of Idaho.
The above set out codes are hereby adopted by the City of New Plymouth to
provide for the regulations set forth herein and to provide for the issuance of
permits and collection of fees therefor. Copies of those documents are on file
in the Office of the City Clerk and by reference are hereby made a part of this
Code as if set out in full verbatim. Any violation shall be subject to the
penalties set forth in section
4-1-4 of this chapter. (Ord. 371, 2-5-2018; amd. Ord. 408, 12-21- 2020)
4-1-2: BUILDING PERMITS:
No person shall commence construction on any structure or building having a
roof supported by columns, poles or walls and designed or intended for shelter,
support, enclosure, or protection of persons, animals, or chattels, of two
hundred (200) square feet or greater, until that person has first secured a
building permit from the City building official, City Clerk or the designated
official and has paid the required fee for the permit.
No person shall commence construction on, set, erect or install any structure,
building or edifice which requires location on the ground or attachment to
something having a fixed location on the ground, portable or nonportable, until
that person has first obtained or has first secured a building permit from the
City building official, City Clerk or the designated official and has paid the
required fee for the permit. Structures include, but are not limited to, mobile
homes, modular homes, carports, walls, billboards, houses, awnings,
outbuildings and communication towers. (Ord. 339, 3-3-2014)
4-1-3: PERMIT FEES 1 :
Any application for a permit shall be accompanied by a fee established in
accordance with a schedule adopted by a resolution of the City Council. No
permit shall become effective until the required fee is paid. (Ord. 248, 6-15-
1998; amd. Ord. 339, 3-3-2014)
 
Notes
1 1. The schedule of permit fees can be found on file in the City Clerk's
  Office.
4-1-4: PENALTY:
In addition to any penalties provided for within the Building Code or any other
adopted code, the City specifically sets forth the following additional
penalties and provisions:
   (A)   Any person, firm or corporation violating any of the provisions of the
code shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor, and each such person shall be
deemed guilty of a separate offense for each and every day or portion thereof
during which any violation of any of the provisions of the code is committed,
continued, or permitted and upon conviction of any such violation such person
shall be guilty of a misdemeanor punishable in accordance with the general
misdemeanor statutes of the State of Idaho.
   (B)   Should it be necessary for the City to enforce any of the provisions
of this chapter, all costs incurred in enforcement shall be borne by the person
or persons violating this chapter, jointly or severally with the owner of the
property upon which the construction is taking place. Costs shall include:
costs of notice, repair, removal, court costs and attorney fees. (Ord. 371, 2-
5-2018)

PLUMBING CODE
(Rep. by Ord. 248, 6-15-1998)
CHAPTER 3
ELECTRICAL CODE
(Rep. by Ord. 248, 6-15-1998)

GAS REGULATIONS
