It shall be unlawful for any person to allow any water to flow into or upon any
public thoroughfare. (Ord. 106, 1-7-1974)
6-1-48: WINDOWSILLS TO BE KEPT CLEAR:
It shall be unlawful for any person to place or keep on any windowsill, porch
or other projection above the first story of any building abutting on any
sidewalk any article which might do injury by falling upon any person on the
sidewalk in front of such building, unless said article is securely fastened or
protected by screens. (Ord. 106, 1-7-1974)
6-1-49: CONDUCT ON DRIVE-IN PREMISES:
No person on the premises of a drive-in restaurant, bank, theater, business,
public parking facility or other public or private property where parking or
drive-in facilities are offered and extended to the public for use shall
needlessly do any of the following: race the motor vehicle; bring any motor
vehicle to a sudden start or stop; impede the orderly movement of vehicles of
pedestrian traffic on such premises; blow horn, or make or cause to be made any
loud, boisterous, rude, indecent, unseemly or unnecessary noise; speak rude,
indecent, vulgar or profane words toward another person; deface or damage the
property of another; or commit any other act constituting nuisance or
disturbance on said premises whereby the quiet and good order of the premises
or the neighborhood is disturbed.
No person or persons driving or maneuvering a vehicle in a reckless manner
without due care, prudence with lack of caution wherein the driving of said
vehicle in this manner could cause injury to life and property.
Any person who violates any of the provisions of this section or fails to
comply with any of the terms and conditions of this section shall be guilty of
a misdemeanor.
The provisions of this section are hereby declared to be severable and if any
provisions of this section or the application of such provisions to any person
or circumstance is declared invalid for any reason, such declaration shall not
affect the validity of the remaining portions of this section. (Ord. 106, 1-7-
1974)
6-1-50: REFUSAL TO LEAVE REAL PROPERTY:
Any person, except under a landlord-tenant relationship, who, being first
notified either verbally or in writing, by the owner, agent or a designee
thereof, to immediately depart from certain real property and who: a) refuses
to depart after being so notified, or b) returns to the property within thirty
(30) days after expulsion without the owner's, agent's or designee's
permission, is guilty of a misdemeanor, punishable by a fine not to exceed
three hundred dollars ($300.00) or thirty (30) days in jail, or both fine and
jail. (Ord. 229, 9-16-1996)
6-1-51: WINDOW PEEPING:
It shall be unlawful for any person, without first obtaining permission of the
person or persons in lawful possession of any premises upon which a residential
dwelling is located, to enter upon the premises of another for the purpose of
looking, peeking, staring or peeping in the windows of said residence. A
violation of this section shall be a misdemeanor, punishable by a fine not to
exceed three hundred dollars ($300.00) or six (6) months in jail, or both fine
and jail. (Ord. 229, 9-16-1996)

Penalty

6-2-33: Feral Cats
6-2-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, each of the terms defined shall have the meanings
given in this section unless a different meaning is clearly required by the
context. The word "shall" is mandatory, not directory.
ABUSE: Any case in which an animal has been the victim of intentional or
negligent conduct resulting in the animal's bruising, bleeding, malnutrition,
dehydration, burns, fractures or breaks of any bones, subdural hematoma, soft
tissue swelling or death.
AT LARGE: Off the premises of the owner, and not under the control of the owner
or a member of his immediate family either by leash, cord, chain or as
otherwise provided for in this chapter.
ENCLOSURE: A fence or structure of at least six feet (6') in height, forming or
causing containment suitable to prevent the entry of young children, and
suitable to confine an animal in conjunction with other measures which may be
taken by the owner such as tethering of the animal. Such enclosure shall be
securely enclosed and locked and designed with secure sides, top and bottom and
shall be designed to prevent the animal from escaping from the enclosure.
FERAL CAT: A feral cat is a free-ranging small animal domestic feline not
identified by collar, clipped ears, tattoo, or other marking to indicate
ownership, that roams outdoors without any restriction, generally avoids human
contact or otherwise does not allow itself to be handled or touched, and
usually remains hidden from humans.
IMPOUNDED: Taken into custody by any law enforcement agency or person
authorized by the City of New Plymouth.
KENNEL: Any lot or premises or portion thereof on which four (4) or more dogs,
cats or any combination thereof, are maintained, harbored, possessed, bred or
cared for and are not for sale or compensation.
KENNEL, COMMERCIAL: Any lot or premises or portion thereof, on which four (4)
or more dogs, cats or other household domestic animals, or any combination
thereof, are maintained, harbored, possessed, boarded, bred or cared for in
return for compensation or kept for sale.
LARGE ANIMAL: Large animals shall include:
   (A)   Ruminants:
       1.   Bovine (cattle).
      2.   Caprine (goat).
      3.   Ovine (sheep).
   (B)   Equine (horses, mules).
   (C)   Porcine (swine).
   (D)   Feline (large exotic cats).
   (E)   Other unscheduled animals with adult weight over one hundred (100)
pounds.
OWNER: Any person or persons keeping, harboring, possessing, caring for, or
having custodial duties over any animal. Any person who continually feeds and/
or shelters a feral cat shall be considered its owner.
SENIOR CITIZEN: Any person who has attained the age of sixty (60) or older.
SMALL ANIMALS: Small animals shall include:
   (A)   Canine (dog, fox, coyote, etc.).
   (B)   Feline (domestic and small exotic cats).
   (C)   Primates.
   (D)   Avian (chickens, turkeys, waterfowl and exotic birds).
   (E)   Reptiles.
   (F)   Rodents (rabbits, hamsters, etc.).
VICIOUS ANIMAL: (A) Any animal which, when unprovoked in a vicious or
terrorizing manner, approaches any person in apparent attitude of attack upon
the streets, sidewalks, any public grounds or places, or private property not
owned or possessed by the owner of the animal; or
   (B)   Any animal with a known propensity, tendency or disposition to attack
unprovoked, to cause injury or to otherwise endanger the safety of human beings
or domestic animals; or
   (C)   Any animal which bites, inflicts injury, assaults or otherwise attacks
a human being or domestic animal without provocation; or
   (D)   Any animal owned or harbored primarily or in part for the purpose of
fighting or any animal trained for fighting; or
   (E)   Guard dog.
Notwithstanding the definition of a "vicious animal" herein, no animal may be
declared vicious if any injury or damage is sustained by a person who, at the
time of such injury or damage was sustained, was committing a willful trespass
or other tort upon the premises occupied by the owner of the animal, or was
teasing, tormenting, abusing or assaulting the animal or was committing or
attempting to commit a crime.
No animal may be declared vicious if the injury or damage was sustained as a
result of teasing, tormenting, abusing or assaulting the animal. No animal may
be declared vicious if the animal was protecting or defending a human being
within the immediate vicinity of the animal from an unjustified attack or
assault.
There is a rebuttable presumption that a child of less than seven (7) years of
age is not capable of teasing, tormenting, abusing or assaulting or provoking
an animal or willfully trespassing. (Ord. 392, 5-6-2019)
6-2-2: LICENSE REQUIRED:
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to own, harbor, keep or possess a
dog within the city without first procuring a license therefor, as provided by
this chapter, provided however, that the provisions of this chapter shall not
apply to any person visiting in the city for a period not exceeding thirty (30)
days, and owning or possessing a dog, if such dog is:
      1.   Currently licensed and bearing the license issued by another
municipality.
   (B)   Whenever a person shall be found guilty of violating this section,
they shall be fined as follows:
      First offense shall be an infraction and subject to a fine of not less
than twenty dollars ($20.00).
      Second offense within twelve (12) months shall be an infraction and
subject to a fine of not less than fifty dollars ($50.00).
      Third offense within twelve (12) months shall be a misdemeanor and shall
be subject to a fine of not less than one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00).
(Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-3: COLLAR AND TAG REQUIRED:
Every dog shall wear at all times a substantial and durable collar, to which
shall be securely attached the required license tag. The shape of the tag shall
be changed each year and shall have stamped thereon the year for which said tag
was issued and a number that will correspond with the number on the
certificate. (Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-4: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE AND LICENSE FEES:
   (A)   All dogs over six (6) months old shall be licensed. The owner or
person having charge of any dog within the city limits shall make application
to the city clerk and pay a license fee in the sum of ten dollars ($10.00) for
each spayed female or neutered male owned, or the sum of fifteen dollars
($15.00) for every female or male dog which is not spayed or neutered. At the
time of application evidence must be provided of proof of spaying or neutering
from a licensed and qualified veterinarian. Senior citizens will receive
licenses for their spayed or neutered dog for five dollars ($5.00). Licenses
provided for herein shall be valid for a period of one year. Licenses lasting
for three (3) years shall be available upon a payment of thirty dollars
($30.00) for each spayed female or neutered male, forty five dollars ($45.00)
for every female or male dog which is not spayed or neutered and fifteen
dollars ($15.00) for seniors who license their spayed or neutered dog. License
fees shall be waived for any guide dog or certified service dog that has been
properly trained for the purpose of and is used to guide a blind or partially
blind person, a person with impaired hearing, or any other severely disabled
person who requires a certified service dog.
   (B)   The owner shall state at the time application is made for such license
upon printed forms provided for such purpose, his name and address; shall
describe the dog to be licensed in such a manner that the dog may be identified
with reasonable certainty.
   (C)   All dogs shall be licensed for and by the calendar year of January 1
through December 31. Any application for a license for any animal over six (6)
months old must have proof of rabies vaccination. For dogs that are being
licensed for the first time, the fees required pursuant to this chapter shall
be paid no later than December 31 of each calendar year. For dogs that have
previously been licensed in the city, fees shall be paid no later than March 1.
Any person who does not register their dog and pay the fee by March 1 shall be
subject to a ten dollar ($10.00) late fee.
   (D)   Upon satisfactory proof that a license tag has been lost, a new tag of
a different number may be issued by the city clerk upon payment of a fee of
five dollars ($5.00) and the transaction shall be noted upon the city office
files for the number that was originally issued. (Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-5: IMITATION LICENSE TAGS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to allow any dog owned, kept or harbored by
him to wear a license tag received on accounts for any other licensed dog or to
wear any imitation of a license tag issued by the city of that year, or any
other tag marked on the plate or collar similar to that required by the city at
that time and calculated to deceive. Any person who violates this section shall
be guilty of an infraction and fined not less than fifty dollars ($50.00).
(Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-6: DOGS RUNNING AT LARGE PROHIBITED:
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any owner to allow or permit any dog whether
licensed or not to be or remain upon the streets or alleys of the City or in a
public place in the City or off the owner's premises and upon the premises of
another without the consent of the person in possession of such other premises
unless:
      1.   Such dog be in the charge of a person and controlled by a leash not
exceeding ten feet (10') in length.
      2.   Such dog be confined in a motor vehicle.
   (B)   The first time a dog shall be found running at large in violation of
this section, a complaint shall be lodged with the law enforcement agency in
charge of enforcing City ordinances. Upon such a complaint, a written warning
shall be issued to the owner of the dog or to the person who is then in control
of the dog.
   (C)   A second or subsequent time that a dog is found to be running at large
in violation of this section and after a written warning has been provided, any
peace officer observing the dog running at large in violation of this section
or who receives a complaint about the dog running at large, shall have the
authority to issue a citation to the animal's owner or to the person in control
of the dog. Whenever a person shall be found guilty of violating this section,
he shall be fined as follows:
      First offense shall be an infraction punishable by a fine not to exceed
twenty five dollars ($25.00).
      Second offense within twelve (12) months shall be an infraction
punishable by a fine not to exceed fifty dollars ($50.00).
      Third or subsequent offense within twelve (12) months shall be an
infraction punishable by a fine not to exceed one hundred dollars ($100.00).
It shall be no defense that a person has exchanged dogs since the date of the
last offense. (Ord. 383, 7-16-2018)
6-2-7: ANIMALS OR FOWL RUNNING AT LARGE PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to keep any and all horses, mules, cattle,
sheep, swine, goats, chickens, ducks, geese, turkeys or other fowl or poultry,
or any other animals except domesticated dogs, cats and rabbits, within the
City limits except as hereinafter provided:
   (A)   Such animals may be allowed to be kept in areas of the City that are
not served by streets or alleys, and including areas zoned as industrial or
commercial, providing the keeping of such animals in said areas does not
interfere with the enjoyment of homes and parties living adjacent herein.
   (B)   And providing further that the owner or keeper of any said animal
first procures a license to keep such animals in said areas designated herein.
   (C)   The owner or keeper of any of said animals shall make application to
the City Clerk and pay a license fee of five dollars ($5.00) for each large
animal over three (3) months old and five dollars ($5.00) per category for
small animals unless otherwise scheduled per calendar year, or part thereof;
the owner or keeper shall state at the time the application is made for such
license, upon printed forms provided for such purpose, his name and address and
the type and number of animals to be licensed.
   (D)   The person to whom the application is made may designate a person to
inspect the area of the City in which the applicant requests license to keep
animals, to ensure such special use will not interfere with use and enjoyment
of homes and premises adjacent to such property to be so used.
Animals shall not be permitted to run at large in the City at any time during
the year; and it shall be unlawful for anyone to herd or drive any animal
through the streets of the City without having said animal under control by
means of rope, strap or other device by which it may be led, unless such animal
is being driven in harness or hauled; it shall be the duty of any law
enforcement officer designated by the City to seize and impound any and all
horses, mules, cattle, sheep, goats, chickens, ducks, geese, turkeys or other
animals, fowl or poultry found running at large or herded within the aforesaid
City limits. (Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-8: COMMERCIAL KENNELS PROHIBITED:
   (A)   The keeping of any commercial kennel within the City limits is hereby
absolutely prohibited. A "commercial kennel" is hereby defined as any
establishment where dogs are cared for, boarded or kept for hire.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful to keep, maintain or possess upon the premises of
any one household more than four (4) dogs. Provided further, that in the event
the number of dogs upon the premises of any one household exceeds the number of
four (4) for the reason that newborn puppies have been born to a dog living on
said premises, then and in that event, it shall be lawful to keep, maintain and
possess upon said premises, said puppies until they reach the age of three (3)
months.
   (C)   It shall be unlawful to maintain more than four (4) large animals
within the City except on property zoned Agricultural R. (Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-9: RABIES:
The animal control officer or any other law enforcement officer designated by
the city shall have the authority to order the owner of any dog which has
bitten any person in such a manner so as to cause an abrasion of the skin to
place the dog in quarantine in the city pound or any other secure facility for
quarantine for a period of ten (10) days. If such dog shall be determined free
from rabies, the same shall be returned to the owner upon payment of a twenty
five dollar ($25.00) impound fee and a ten dollar ($10.00) charge for each day
the dog has been impounded. No other fee shall be charged. If such fee is not
paid, the dog shall be subject to disposal after proper notice is given to the
owner provided that the owner can be located. (Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-10: ENFORCEMENT:
   (A)   The enforcement of this chapter shall be the responsibility of the law
enforcement agency employed by the city for law enforcement purpose. That
agency may designate an animal control officer and give him/her the authority
of a police officer. Such officer shall be responsible to the appointed law
enforcement agency for the enforcement of all animal control regulations.
   (B)   All fees collected shall be turned over to the city clerk. (Ord. 354,
11-7-2016)
6-2-11: INTERFERENCE WITH ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to hinder, molest or in any way interfere
with the animal control officer, any law enforcement officer or any other
person designated and acting on behalf of the city, while they are lawfully
engaged in the performance of their duties pursuant to this chapter. (Ord. 354,
11-7-2016)
6-2-12: DISTURBING THE PEACE:
No person owning any dog shall suffer or permit any such dog to disturb the
peace and quiet of a neighborhood by howling, barking, making loud or unusual
noises, or by running through or across cultivated gardens or fields. (Ord.
354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-13: NUISANCES:
   (A)   Nuisance Declared: Any animal is hereby declared to be a public
nuisance if it:
      1.   Bites a person.
      2.   Chases vehicles or persons.
      3.   Damages or destroys property of persons other than the owner of the
animal.
      4.   Scatters garbage.
      5.   Trespasses on private property of persons other than the owner of
the animal.
      6.   Barks or howls or whines for five (5) or more total minutes in any
fifteen (15) consecutive minutes and thereby disturbs one or more persons not
then residing in the residence of the owner, possessor or keeper of the animal;
provided, however, an initial occurrence shall result in the issuance of a
warning only with any subsequent occurrence within a seven (7) day calendar
period of the initial occurrence being subject to all penalties provided for
herein.
      7.   Makes unprovoked attacks on other animals.
      8.   Any biting animal may be declared vicious by the animal control
board.
   (B)   Exception To Dog As Public Nuisance: A dog shall not be considered a
public nuisance if the dog bites:
      1.   A person battering a dog's owner or the owner's spouse or children
or persons legally residing with the owner, or
      2.   A person wrongfully assaulting the dog, or
      3.   A person entering a fully fenced area, regardless of where located,
if that area is conspicuously posted with signs warning of the presence of the
dog within the fenced area. (Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-14: ANIMAL WASTE MATTER:
It shall be unlawful for a person owning or keeping an animal to allow the
animal to deposit solid waste matter on any property other than that of the
person owning or keeping the animal, but it shall be a defense to this action
if the owner or keeper removes the solid waste and properly disposes of it.
(Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-15: IMPOUNDING:
   (A)   It shall be the duty of the city's appointed law enforcement agency or
the designated animal control officer to apprehend any animal found running at
large contrary to the provisions of this chapter, and to impound such animal in
the city pound or other suitable facility; provided that if a fierce, dangerous
or vicious animal found running at large cannot be safely taken up and
impounded, such animal may be slain by any police officer or the animal control
officer of the city.
   (B)   The city's appointed law enforcement agency or the designated animal
control officer so impounding or slaying any animal shall record a description
of the animal, whether licensed or not in a book kept for that purpose.
   (C)   If the animal is licensed and shall be wearing a license tag when
apprehended or slain, the law enforcement officer or animal control officer
shall also record the name and address of the owner and the number of the tag.
(Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-16: CITY POUND:
The city is hereby authorized and empowered, but not required, to secure and
maintain a suitable pound for the purpose of carrying out the provisions of
this chapter. The city's law enforcement officers or the animal control officer
will be the sole judge of how animals are to be segregated and penned. (Ord.
354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-17: ANIMALS IMPOUNDED:
   (A)   The owner or owners of any animals impounded may redeem the same by
paying all the costs, charges and penalties assessed, if any, that have accrued
up to the time of making the redemption, and when the same are paid, it shall
be the duty of the animal control officer or any other designated law
enforcement officer to release the animal from said pound to the said owner
thereof. The owner of said animal shall pay an impound fee of twenty five
dollars ($25.00) together with a ten dollar ($10.00) per day boarding fee.
   (B)   All fees and boarding services for the taking up of such animals shall
be payable to and collected by the city clerk. (Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-18: LICENSED DOGS IMPOUNDED:
It shall be the duty of the designated law enforcement officer or any other
person designated by the city to cause notice to be served either in person or
by mail upon the registered owner of any licensed dog impounded under the
provisions of this chapter. Any dog not redeemed is declared to be a public
nuisance and may be disposed of in a humane manner under the direction of the
designated law enforcement officer, within five (5) days of notification. (Ord.
354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-19: UNLICENSED DOGS IMPOUNDED:
It shall be the duty of the designated law enforcement agency or any other
person designated by the city to hold for a period of three (3) working days
any unlicensed dog impounded under the provisions of this chapter. Any such
unlicensed dog not redeemed within said three (3) day period shall be declared
to be a stray dog and a public nuisance and may be disposed of in a humane
manner under the direction of the law enforcement agency designated to act on
behalf of the city. (Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-20: NOTICE OF SALE OF ANIMALS:
If the owner or person entitled to the possession of any large animal does not
pay the charges and does not take said animal away within five (5) days from
the time it is taken into custody, the designated law enforcement agency for
the city may sell such animal at public auction after having given at least
five (5) days' notice of the time and place of such sale by publishing or by
posting said notice in three (3) public places in the municipality as well as
serving a copy of said notice upon the owner or possessor, if known, of said
animal. Such animal may be redeemed at any time before the date of sale by the
payment to the city clerk of any fees, expenses and charges herein provided.
All revenue from sale shall become part of the general fund of the city. (Ord.
354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-21: FREEING OF IMPOUNDED ANIMALS AND POULTRY PROHIBITED:
   (A)   It shall be unlawful to break upon or in any manner directly or
indirectly, aid or assist in the breaking open of or into any pen or enclosure
with intent of releasing any animal or poultry.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person except those responsible for the
enforcement of this chapter to release any animal from the city pound or from
any other place where an animal may be held for observation. (Ord. 354, 11-7-
2016)
6-2-22: LIVESTOCK WITHIN PUBLIC PARKS:
Except during those days which are designated as Payette County Fair week, no
large animal of any kind shall be allowed within any public park within the
city except when such animal is kept upon the regularly traveled motor vehicle
public rights of way within said park. (Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-23: LARGE ANIMALS PROHIBITED ON SIDEWALKS AND CERTAIN STREETS:
Except during those days which are designated as Payette County Fair week, it
shall be unlawful and prohibited for horsedrawn vehicles or the riding of
horses on all sidewalks of all streets and upon any street or alley which has
been newly oiled, paved or laid with concrete. (Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-24: CRUELTY TO ANIMALS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to torture or beat cruelly, starve, or
otherwise ill treat any animal in his care or charge, whether belonging to
himself or any other person. (Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-25: DOG OR COCK FIGHTS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to participate in any dog or cock fights
within the limits of the city. (Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-26: DETERMINATION OF A VICIOUS ANIMAL:
   (A)   There is hereby created a standing animal control board. The standing
animal control board shall be appointed by the mayor and confirmed by the
council. The standing animal control board shall consist of a council member, a
law enforcement officer and two (2) citizens. The standing animal control board
shall meet as often as may be directed by the mayor or city council, but not
less than quarterly. In the event the animal control board is required to
review the actions of any animal and make a determination that an animal is
vicious or is not vicious, the animal control board shall be increased to
include the owner of the animal subject to a review and a person who has been
damaged by the animal.
   (B)   Where there is reason to believe that an animal has acted in such a
manner that it should be declared vicious, the person wishing to have the
animal declared vicious shall file a written request with the city clerk asking
that the city convene the animal control board to review the actions of the
animal.
   (C)   The owner, possessor or caretaker of the animal shall be notified of
the request and shall be notified that the person has the right to object to an
animal being found vicious. The person filing the request and the owner, keeper
or caretaker of the animal shall have the right to appear at the time and place
set for the hearing and provide testimony regarding whether the animal should
or should not be declared to be a vicious animal.
   (D)   After a hearing the animal control board shall make a determination if
the animal is vicious or not vicious.
   (E)   In the event that the animal control board has declared an animal
vicious, the owner, possessor or caretaker of the animal shall be notified in
writing of this determination. The owner, possessor or caretaker of the animal
shall be notified that they have the right within five (5) days of a
determination to appeal a decision by filing a written petition challenging the
determination. If the owner of the animal contests the determination, he or she
may, within five (5) days of such determination, bring a petition to the mayor
and city council. The city council shall conduct a hearing de novo and make its
own determination as to viciousness. Said hearing shall be conducted within
fourteen (14) days of the petition. The city council may decide all issues for
or against the owner of the animal regardless of the fact that said owner fails
to appear at said hearing.
   (F)   The determination of the city council shall be final and conclusive
upon all parties thereto. A finding that the animal is not vicious does not
preclude the animal control board from making a later determination that the
animal is vicious based upon subsequent actions of the animal.
   (G)   In the event the animal control officer or a law enforcement officer
has probable cause to believe that an animal is vicious and may pose a threat
of serious harm to human beings or other domestic animals if the animal is
allowed to remain at large, they may seize and impound the animal pending the
aforesaid hearings. The owner of the animal shall be liable to the city for the
costs and expenses of impoundment of such animal. (Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-27: VICIOUS ANIMALS:
   (A)   No dog or other animal that has been declared to be vicious by the
animal control board shall remain in, visit or be kept within the city limits
of the city of New Plymouth.
   (B)   In the event that the owner of a vicious animal refuses to surrender
the animal to the law enforcement agency designated by the city or to the
animal control officer, the city may seek a search warrant or any other
appropriate warrant or order from a magistrate judge of the district court and
seize the animal upon execution of the warrant. (Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-28: PURPOSE OR INTENT; HARBORING:
   (A)   No person shall own or harbor any animal for the purpose of animal
fighting, or training, torment, badger, bait or use any animal for the purpose
of causing or encouraging said animal to make unprovoked attacks upon human
beings or domestic animals.
   (B)   No person shall possess with intent to sell, or offer for sale, breed
or buy or attempt to buy within the state any vicious animal. (Ord. 354, 11-7-
2016)
6-2-29: COMMANDING AN ANIMAL TO ATTACK; PROHIBITED:
Except where great bodily harm or death is likely to immediately ensue, it
shall be unlawful for any person to command, encourage or aid by word or
conduct, any animal to bite, chase, attack or attempt to bite, chase or attack,
another person or animal. (Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-30: ACTION FOR DAMAGES; DESTRUCTION OF OFFENDING VICIOUS ANIMAL; CIVIL
PENALTY:
If any vicious animal shall, when unprovoked, kill or wound, or assist in
killing or wounding any sheep, lamb, cattle, horse, hog, swine, fowl or other
domestic animal, belonging to or in the possession of any person, or shall,
when unprovoked, attack, assault, bite or otherwise injure any human being or
assist in attacking, assaulting, biting or otherwise injuring any human being
while out of or within the enclosure of the owner or keeper of such vicious
animal, or while otherwise on or off the property of the owner whether or not
such vicious animal was on a leash and securely muzzled or whether the vicious
animal escaped without fault of the owner or keeper, the owner or keeper of
such animal shall be liable to the person aggrieved as aforesaid, for all
damages sustained, to be recovered in a civil action, with costs of suit. It is
rebuttably presumed as a matter of law that the owning, keeping or harboring of
a vicious animal in violation of this chapter is a nuisance. It shall not be
necessary, in order to sustain any such action, to prove that the owner of such
vicious animal knew that such vicious animal possessed the propensity to cause
such damage or that the vicious animal had a vicious nature. Upon such attack
or assault, the designated law enforcement agency for the city is hereby
empowered to confiscate and destroy such vicious animal, if the conduct of such
vicious animal or its owner constituted a violation of the provisions of this
chapter, punishable by the confiscation and destruction of the animal. (Ord.
354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-31: LIABILITY OF PARENTS FOR DAMAGES BY ANIMAL OWNED BY MINOR:
In the event that the owner of the vicious animal is a minor, the parent or
guardian of such minor shall be liable for all injuries and property damage
sustained by any person or domestic animal abused by an unprovoked attack by
said vicious animal. (Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-32: VICIOUS ANIMALS PROHIBITED:
   (A)   Vicious Animals:
      1.   No animal which has been declared vicious by the animal control
board shall come into, remain in or be found in the city limits.
Any animal which has been declared vicious by the animal control board and
which is found within the city limits shall be confiscated and destroyed in an
expeditious and humane manner after the expiration of a five (5) day waiting
period exclusive of Sundays and holidays. In addition, the owner shall be
guilty of a misdemeanor and shall pay a two hundred fifty dollar ($250.00)
fine.
      2.   If any vicious animal shall, when unprovoked, kill, wound, or assist
in killing or wounding any animal, the owner of said animal shall pay a two
hundred fifty dollar ($250.00) fine and the animal control officer is empowered
to confiscate and, after the expiration of a five (5) day waiting period
exclusive of Sundays and holidays, shall destroy said vicious animal. For each
subsequent violation the same owner of another vicious animal shall pay a fine
of three hundred dollars ($300.00).
      3.   If any vicious animal shall, when unprovoked, attack, assault,
wound, bite or otherwise injure or kill a human being, the owner shall pay a
five hundred dollar ($500.00) fine and the animal control officer is empowered
to and shall confiscate and, after the expiration of a five (5) day waiting
period exclusive of Sundays and holidays, shall destroy said vicious animal.
      4.   If any animal owner objects to the destruction of an animal pursuant
to this section, he/she shall file a petition with the Mayor or City Clerk and
a hearing on the merits shall be had before the City Council within fourteen
(14) days. The decision of the City Council shall be final and binding on all
parties.
      5.   A violation of either section
6-2-24, "Cruelty To Animals", or
6-2-25, "Dog Or Cock Fights", of this chapter shall be a misdemeanor punishable
by not less than thirty (30) days in the Payette County Jail and a fine of not
less than three hundred dollars ($300.00) but not more than one year in the
Payette County Jail or a fine of not more than one thousand dollars
($1,000.00).
      6.   Unless other penalties for specific acts are provided in the body of
this chapter, any violation of this chapter shall be a misdemeanor punishable
in accordance with the General Misdemeanor Statutes of the State.
      7.   No fine shall be suspended by any court of competent jurisdiction.
(Ord. 354, 11-7-2016)
6-2-33: FERAL CATS:
   (A)   Feral cats are hereby declared to be a public nuisance.
   (B)   Feeding or sheltering feral cats is a violation of this section unless
the person doing so establishes to the City that he or she is working with a
licensed veterinarian to spay or neuter the cats in their care and provides to
the City documentation of such sterilization.
   (C)   It shall be unlawful for any person to own, keep, hold, board, feed or
harbor more than five (5) feral cats.
   (D)   Feeding or sheltering feral cats in violation of this section shall
constitute a public nuisance the abatement of which may be accomplished by the
seizure of, whether on public or private property, and/or the destruction of
such feral cats, or by any other means of abatement of a public nuisance
authorized by law.
   (E)   This section is not intended to prevent a private party from asserting
any legal rights he or she may have to enjoin or seek damages against a person
sheltering or feeding feral cats.
   (F)   Violation of this section shall constitute a misdemeanor. (Ord. 392,
5-6-2019)
CHAPTER 3
DOGS, ANIMALS
(Rep. by Ord. 116, 10-4-1976)
CHAPTER 4
ABANDONED CONTAINERS
SECTION:
6-4-1: Unlawful Act
6-4-1: UNLAWFUL ACT:
It shall be unlawful for any person to leave or permit to remain outside of any
dwelling, building or other structure, or within any unoccupied or abandoned
building, structure or dwelling under his control, in a place accessible to
children, any abandoned, unattended or discarded ice box, refrigerator or other
container which has a door or lid, snaplock or other locking device which may
not be released from the inside, without first removing said door or lid,
snaplock or other locking device. (1960 Code)
CHAPTER 5
AIR GUNS, FIREARMS
SECTION:
6-5-1: Definitions
6-5-2: Concealed Weapons (Rep. by Ord. 358, 6-5-2017)
6-5-3: Discharge Of Firearms Prohibited
6-5-4: Exceptions; Permits
6-5-5: Bow And Arrow, Blowgun Or Dart Gun Within City Limits
6-5-6: Bow And Arrow Permits
6-5-7: Insurance Required
6-5-8: Penalty
6-5-1: DEFINITIONS:
Wherever the term "firearms" is used in this chapter, the term shall mean any
instrument used in the propulsion of shot, shell or bullets or other harmful
objects by the action of gunpowder exploded within it, or by the action of
compressed air within it, or by the power of springs and including what are
commonly known as air rifles and BB guns. (Ord. 151, 2-1-1982, eff. 2-11-1982)
6-5-2: CONCEALED WEAPONS:
(Rep. by Ord. 358, 6-5-2017)
6-5-3: DISCHARGE OF FIREARMS PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge firearms of any kind or
description within the limits of the Municipality; provided, however, that this
shall not apply to police officers in the discharge of their duties or to
private citizens acting in defense of themselves, others or in defense of their
property; provided further that this prohibition shall not apply to City of New
Plymouth Public Works employees while acting in the scope of their employment
within the City limits and while discharging firearms to eradicate, eliminate,
control or kill rock chucks, marmots or other vermin. (Ord. 351, 7-18-2016)
6-5-4: EXCEPTIONS; PERMITS:
The Governing Body may at any time, upon receipt of proper application, grant
permits to shooting galleries, gun clubs and others for shooting in fixed
localities and under specified rules. Such permits shall be in writing attested
by the Clerk conforming to such requirements as the Governing Body shall
demand, and the permit thus issued shall be subject to revocation at any time
by action of the Governing Body. (Ord. 151, 2-1-1982, eff. 2-11-1982)
6-5-5: BOW AND ARROW, BLOWGUN OR DART GUN WITHIN CITY LIMITS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge or shoot an arrow from any bow
or discharge a dart, pellet or other projectile from a blowgun or a dart gun in
the City limits without first securing a permit from the City.
A violation of this section shall be a misdemeanor, punishable by a fine not to
exceed three hundred dollars ($300.00) or six (6) months in jail, or both fine
and jail. (Ord. 233, 1-6-1997)
6-5-6: BOW AND ARROW PERMITS:
Permits may be secured after application to the City police, or any agency
authorized by the City Council when it is demonstrated by the applicant that
the bow and arrow to be used is a toy and use poses no danger to any person or
property or that use is pursuant to some organized course of instruction, or
that use will be conducted in such a manner that no person or property will be
endangered. Issuance of permits is discretionary with the issuing authority,
may be of any term, length or duration, and shall terminate, automatically,
without notice of any kind at the time set in the permit. (Ord. 151, 2-1-1982,
eff. 2-11-1982)
6-5-7: INSURANCE REQUIRED:
The issuing authority may withhold issuance of a permit until such time as
applicant signs an indemnity agreement holding the City harmless from any
damage which may arise from the use of the bow and arrow and shows proof of
coverage for liability insurance in an amount not to exceed one hundred
thousand dollars ($100,000.00). (Ord. 151, 2-1-1982, eff. 2-11-1982)
6-5-8: PENALTY:
Any person who violates any section of this chapter shall be punished by a fine
not to exceed three hundred dollars ($300.00) or by imprisonment in the County
Jail not to exceed three (3) months or by both fine and imprisonment. (Ord.
151, 2-1-1982, eff. 2-11-1982)
CHAPTER 6
MINORS
SECTION:
6-6-1: Runaways
6-6-2: Curfew
6-6-3: Encourage Delinquency
6-6-4: Violation, Penalty
6-6-1: RUNAWAYS:
It is unlawful for any child under eighteen (18) years of age who lives,
resides or is present within the city of New Plymouth to: a) run away or
attempt to run away from their parents, custodial parent, guardian or other
legally appointed custodian; b) to be present within the city limits after
having run away from their parents, custodial parent, guardian or other legally
appointed custodian while residing in another city; c) to do any act which
places the child beyond the control of their parents, custodial parent,
guardian or other legally appointed custodian; d) aid or abet any child in
being a runaway; e) fail to report to law enforcement or to the department of
health and welfare the whereabouts of a child who has violated this section
knowing the child to be in violation hereof. (Ord. 264, 12-4-2000)
6-6-2: CURFEW:
   (A)   Curfew Established:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person under the age of sixteen (16)
years to be or to remain, and it shall be unlawful for any parent, guardian or
other person having the care and custody of any person under the age of sixteen
(16) years to permit such person to be or to remain, in or upon any street,
alley, public ground, public places or any place open to the public or exposed
to public use within New Plymouth, between the hours of eleven o'clock (11:00)
P.M. and five o'clock (5:00) A.M.
      2.   It shall be unlawful for any person from the age of sixteen (16)
years to the age of eighteen (18) years to be or to remain, and it shall be
unlawful for any parent, guardian or other person having the care and custody
of any person between the age of sixteen (16) years to eighteen (18) years to
permit such person to be or to remain in or upon any street, alley, public
ground, public places or any place open to the public or exposed to public use
within New Plymouth, between the hours of twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight and
five o'clock (5:00) A.M.
   (B)   Exceptions: The provisions of subsection (A) of this section shall not
apply to any person who is accompanied by his parent, guardian or other adult
person having the care and custody of him or her nor to any person who is in
the performance of an errand or duty directed by his or her parent, guardian or
other adult person having the care and custody of him or her nor to any person
who is actually at the time engaged in legitimate employment for profit.
   (C)   Evidence Of Violation:
      1.   The presence of a person under the age of sixteen (16) years in or
upon any street, alley, public ground, public places or any place open to the
public or exposed to the public use within the city between the hours of eleven
o'clock (11:00) P.M. and five o'clock (5:00) A.M. not being accompanied by his
parents, guardian or one having legal custody of said child not being in the
performance of an errand or duty directed by his parent, guardian or other
adult person having the care and custody of him, nor being actually engaged in
legitimate employment for profit shall be prima facie evidence of the violation
of this section.
      2.   The presence of a person between the ages of sixteen (16) years and
eighteen (18) years in or upon any street, alley, public ground, public places
or any place open to the public or exposed to public use within the city
between the hours of twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight and five o'clock (5:00)
A.M. not being accompanied by his parent, guardian or one having legal custody
of said child, not being in the performance of an errand or duty directed by
his parent, guardian or other adult person having the care and custody of him
nor being actually engaged in legitimate employment for profit, shall be prima
facie evidence of a violation of this section. (Ord. 139, 3-3-1980)
6-6-3: ENCOURAGE DELINQUENCY:
It shall be unlawful for any person by any act or neglect to encourage, aid or
cause any person under the age of eighteen (18) years to come within the
purview of section
6-6-2 of this chapter. (Ord. 139, 3-3-1980; amd. Ord. 198, 7-16-1990)
6-6-4: VIOLATION, PENALTY:
Violation of this chapter by a minor child shall bring said child within the
purview of the youth rehabilitation act of the state, and violation of this
chapter by an adult shall be punishable by imprisonment in the Payette County
jail for a period not to exceed six (6) months or by a fine not to exceed three
hundred dollars ($300.00), or by both such imprisonment and fine. (Ord. 139, 3-
3-1980)
CHAPTER 7
PLASTIC BAGS OR COVERINGS
SECTION:
6-7-1: Definition
6-7-2: Warning Required
6-7-3: Certain Bags a Nuisance
6-7-1: DEFINITION:
The words "plastic coverings," "plastic bag," or "plastic package" when used in
this Chapter shall mean any covering, package or bag made of plastic material
sufficiently thin and pliable to respond to static electricity created by
contact with the human body to the extent that it clings to the human skin or
body.
6-7-2: WARNING REQUIRED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to have in his possession, or to deliver as
a cover or wrapper, any plastic bag that is of sufficient size to fit over a
child's head, or any bag which, when open has an opening larger than twenty
five (25) square inches or a capacity of more than one hundred twenty five
(125) cubic inches, unless there is at all times clearly printed on such bag or
covering, or on a paper attached to such bag or covering, words in letters at
least one quarter inch (1/4) high as follows:
   WARNING: To avoid danger of suffocation keep this bag (or covering) away
from babies and children. Do not use in cribs, beds, carriages or play pens.
This is not a toy.
6-7-3: CERTAIN BAGS A NUISANCE:
Any plastic bag, covering or package not carrying or accompanied by the printed
warning as provided in Section
6-7-2 of this Chapter is hereby declared a nuisance. (1960 Code)
CHAPTER 8
WRECKED, DISMANTLED OR INOPERATIVE VEHICLES
SECTION:
6-8-1: Definition
6-8-2: Junk Vehicles a Nuisance
6-8-3: Maintenance of Junk Motor Vehicles or Parts Thereof Unlawful
6-8-4: Exemptions
6-8-5: Removal by City
6-8-6: Refusal to Remove Junk Vehicles or Parts Thereof Unlawful
6-8-7: Interference with Removal of Junk Vehicles or Parts Thereof Unlawful
6-8-1: DEFINITION:
A wrecked, dismantled or inoperative vehicle or part thereof, hereinafter
called a junk motor vehicle, shall be defined as an unsightly motor vehicle or
a part or parts therefrom, which meets any one of the following qualifications:
   (A)   It does not carry a current valid state registration and license
plate.
   (B)   It cannot be safely operated under its own power.
   (C)   It does not have any one of the following: Foot brakes, headlights,
taillights, horn, muffler, rear view mirrors, windshield wipers or adequate
fenders.
6-8-2: JUNK VEHICLES A NUISANCE:
The accumulation and storage of junk vehicles or parts thereof on private or
public property is hereby found to create a condition tending to reduce the
value of private property, to promote blight and deterioration, to invite
plundering, to create fire hazards, to constitute an attractive nuisance
creating a hazard to health, and safety to minors, to create a harborage for
rodents and insects and to be injurious to the health, safety and general
welfare. Therefore, the presence of a wrecked, dismantled or inoperative
vehicle or parts thereof on private or public property, except as expressly
hereinafter permitted, is hereby declared to constitute a public nuisance which
may be abated as such in accordance with the provisions of this Section.
6-8-3: MAINTENANCE OF JUNK MOTOR VEHICLES OR PARTS THEREOF UNLAWFUL:
It shall be unlawful for any person or persons, firm, partnership or
corporation to maintain a junk motor vehicle, vehicles, or parts thereof on
residential property or business property for a period of more than thirty (30)
days.
6-8-4: EXEMPTIONS:
This Ordinance shall not apply to:
   (A)   A vehicle or part thereof which is completely enclosed within a
building in a lawful manner where it is not visible from the street or other
public or private property; or
   (B)   A vehicle or part thereof which is stored or parked in a lawful manner
on private property in connection with the business of a licensed dismantler,
licensed vehicle dealer, a junk dealer, or when such storage or parking is
necessary to the operation of a lawfully conducted business or commercial
enterprise; or
   (C)   Any vehicle or vehicles owned by a person or persons serving on active
duty outside the State of Idaho in the armed services of the United States of
America, provided, such vehicle or vehicles did not qualify as a junk motor
vehicle prior to becoming so engaged in such active service.
6-8-5: REMOVAL BY CITY:
The Police Chief, Fire Chief, or Building Inspector or their authorized
representative may order any junk motor vehicle, vehicles or parts thereof
removed within ten (10) days.
Notice of such order shall be placed upon said junk motor vehicle, vehicles or
parts thereof. Copies of said notice shall be served upon any adult occupying
the real estate on which the junk motor vehicle, vehicles or parts thereof are
located and upon the owner of the junk if known. If no occupant of the real
estate or owner of the junk vehicle, vehicles or parts thereof can be found, a
notice affixed to any building on the real estate shall constitute notice to
the owner or occupant of the real estate and to the owners of the junk motor
vehicle, vehicles or parts thereof. If there is no building on the real estate,
said notice may be affixed elsewhere on the real estate.
If said junk vehicle, vehicles, or parts thereof are not removed within the
time so fixed, the Police Chief, Fire Chief or Building Inspector or their
authorized representative may cause said junk vehicle, vehicles or parts
thereof to be removed and the actual costs of removal or tow-in charge and a
storage of not more than one dollar fifty cents ($1.50) per day for so long as
the same is in possession and custody of the City shall be charged to the
owner. In the event said junk motor vehicle, vehicles or parts thereof are not
claimed by the lawful owner, than and in that event the same shall be sold. To
defray the expense of removal of junk motor vehicle, vehicles or parts thereof
the City may levy a special assessment on the land or premises whereon the same
were maintained, as provided under Section 50-334 of the Idaho Code.
6-8-6: REFUSAL TO REMOVE JUNK VEHICLES OR PARTS THEREOF UNLAWFUL:
It shall be unlawful and a misdemeanor for any person to fail or refuse to
remove a wrecked, junk motor vehicle, vehicles or parts thereof or refuse to
abate such nuisance when ordered to do so in accordance with the provisions of
this Ordinance.
6-8-7: INTERFERENCE WITH REMOVAL OF JUNK VEHICLES OR PARTS THEREOF UNLAWFUL:
It shall be unlawful and a misdemeanor to interfere with, hinder, or refuse to
allow any authorized City officer or employee to enter upon private or public
property to enforce the provisions of this Ordinance. (Ord. 109; 1-7-74; Eff.
1-17-74)
CHAPTER 9
STOPPING, STANDING OR PARKING
SECTION:
6-9-1: Definitions
6-9-2: Standing Or Parking Close To Curb
6-9-3: Permit For Loading Or Unloading At Angle To Curb
6-9-4: Vehicle Weight Limits
6-9-5: Stopping Or Parking Prohibited
6-9-6: Restrictions On Parking
6-9-7: Obstructing Traffic
6-9-8: All Night Parking Prohibited
6-9-9: Parking Of Trucks (Rep. by Ord. 285, 3-17-2003)
6-9-10: Parking For Certain Purposes Prohibited
6-9-11: Parking Adjacent To Schools
6-9-12: Parking Prohibited On Narrow Streets
6-9-13: Passenger And Freight Curb Loading Zones
6-9-14: Off Street Parking And Loading
6-9-15: Application Of Provisions
6-9-16: Regulations Not Excluded
6-9-17: Authority To Remove Vehicles
6-9-18: Vehicle Damaged During Removal, Nonliability
6-9-19: Liability For Towing And Storage Charges
6-9-20: City Not Liable
6-9-21: Request Vehicle Removal By Owner
6-9-22: Refusal To Remove Vehicle
6-9-23: Lien Against Vehicle
6-9-24: Removal By City
6-9-25: Vehicles Obstructing Emergency City Services
6-9-26: Parking Or Camping
6-9-27: Violations
6-9-1: DEFINITIONS:
PARKED VEHICLE: Includes, but is not necessarily limited to, any nonmoving
vehicle, whether licensed or unlicensed, functional or disabled.
VEHICLE: As defined by title 49 of the Idaho Code, but shall include all forms
of conveyances whether, motorized or not. (Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-2: STANDING OR PARKING CLOSE TO CURB:
Other than in those areas marked for angle parking, it shall be unlawful to
stand or park a vehicle in a roadway other than parallel with the edge of the
roadway headed in the direction of lawful traffic movement and with the
curbside wheels of the vehicle within eighteen inches (18") of the curb or edge
of the roadway. In any area zoned A, B, or C residential, where a curb is not
installed, it shall be unlawful to park on the maintained roadway surface.
(Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-3: PERMIT FOR LOADING OR UNLOADING AT ANGLE TO CURB:
The clerk or police department are authorized to issue special permits for the
backing of a vehicle to the curb for the purpose of loading or unloading
merchandise or materials subject to the terms and conditions of such permit.
Such permits may be issued either to the owner or lessee of real property or to
the owner or lessee of the vehicle. It shall be unlawful for any permittee or
other person to violate any of the special terms or conditions of any such
permit. (Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-4: VEHICLE WEIGHT LIMITS:
Vehicles exceeding gross weight of nine thousand (9,000) pounds per axle shall
be prohibited from traveling or parking where posted. (Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-5: STOPPING OR PARKING PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to stop or park a vehicle, except in
compliance with or under the direction of a police officer or traffic control
device in any of the following places:
   (A)   On a sidewalk;
   (B)   In front of a public or private driveway;
   (C)   Within an intersection on any roadway surface;
   (D)   Within fifteen feet (15') of a fire hydrant;
   (E)   On a crosswalk;
   (F)   Within fifty feet (50') of the nearest rail of a railroad crossing;
   (G)   Within ten feet (10') of the driveway entrance to any fire station;
   (H)   Alongside or opposite any street obstruction or excavation when
stopping or parking would obstruct traffic;
   (I)   On a roadway side of any vehicle stopped or parked at the edge or curb
of a street;
   (J)   Upon any bridge or other elevated structure upon a highway;
   (K)   At any place where signs prohibit parking or stopping.
It shall be unlawful for any person to move a vehicle not lawfully under his
control into any such prohibited area or farther away from the curb than is
lawful. (Ord. 285, 3-17-2003)
6-9-6: RESTRICTIONS ON PARKING:
   (A)   Council Authority: The city council shall have the authority to impose
a parking time limit or to prohibit parking altogether on any street within the
corporate city limits. When parking restrictions are imposed upon an area, the
council, by motion and simple majority vote, shall designate the areas where
restrictions apply, the type of restrictions which shall be in force and shall
instruct the chief of police or any other city personnel to give notice as set
out below.
   (B)   Truck Parking: It shall be unlawful for any truck having a single axle
of over nine thousand (9,000) GVW when empty, or for any truck with three (3)
or more axles, or any truck or trailer, singly or when in combination, to park
in any residential neighborhood.
   (C)   Outside And Inside Boulevard: It shall be unlawful for any person to
park any motor vehicle in the grass on the city right of way along either the
inside or outside boulevards. An exception may be made by the city council on
those occasions when in the opinion of the council it is in the best interest
of the city to allow such parking.
   (D)   Notice: Notice of any parking restriction shall be adequate if such
notice is posted on the entrances to the city or on any corner of any street
upon which a parking restriction shall be applied.
   (E)   Unlawful Parking: It shall be unlawful for any person to park any
tractor, trailer, truck, recreational vehicle, camper, camper trailer, mobile
home, motor home, double wide, trailer house or semitrailer on the paved
portion of any street or street right of way, when that unit is supported by a
jack, footing, prop, brace, lever or other support that causes steel to rest
directly upon the pavement.
   (F)   Penalty: After parking has been prohibited or parking restrictions
have been imposed and proper signs placed, any person violating the posted
restriction shall be guilty of an infraction. Upon conviction for violating a
parking restriction a person shall be fined not less than fifty dollars
($50.00). (Ord. 285, 3-17-2003)
6-9-7: OBSTRUCTING TRAFFIC:
It shall be unlawful for any person to park any vehicle upon a street, alley or
roadway, in such a manner or under such conditions as to leave available less
than ten feet (10') of the width of the roadway for free movement of vehicular
traffic. (Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-8: ALL NIGHT PARKING PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to park a vehicle overnight where posted.
(Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-9: PARKING OF TRUCKS:
(Rep. by Ord. 285, 3-17-2003)
6-9-10: PARKING FOR CERTAIN PURPOSES PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to park a vehicle upon any roadway or upon
any portion of any road right of way for the purpose of:
   (A)   Displaying such vehicle for sale;
   (B)   Washing, maintaining or repairing such vehicle, except repairs
necessitated by any emergency;
   (C)   Selling merchandise from said vehicle without first obtaining a
license or permit;
   (D)   Displaying a vehicle for rent or lease or advertising any business
without first obtaining a permit from the city council. (Ord. 288, 7-7-2003)
6-9-11: PARKING ADJACENT TO SCHOOLS:
The city is hereby authorized to erect signs indicating no parking upon either
or both sides of any street adjacent to any school property when such parking
would interfere with traffic or create a hazardous situation as determined by
the city council. (Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-12: PARKING PROHIBITED ON NARROW STREETS:
The city is hereby authorized to erect signs indicating no parking upon any
street when the width of the roadway does not exceed twenty feet (20') or upon
one side of a street as indicated by such signs when the width of the roadway
does not exceed thirty feet (30'). (Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-13: PASSENGER AND FREIGHT CURB LOADING ZONES:
   (A)   Loading Or Unloading Only: The City is hereby authorized to determine
the location of passenger and freight curb loading zones and shall place and
maintain appropriate signs indicating the same and stating the hours during
which the provisions of this chapter are applicable.
   (B)   Permits For Curb Loading Zones: The City shall not hereafter designate
or sign any curb loading zone upon special request of any person unless such
person makes application for a permit for such zone and for two (2) signs to
indicate the ends of each zone. Said permit fee shall be set and designated by
the Mayor and Council.
   (C)   Standing In Zones:
      1.   Passenger Curb Loading Zones: It shall be unlawful for any person to
stop, stand or park a vehicle for any purpose or period of time other than the
expeditious loading or unloading of passengers in any place marked as passenger
curb loading zone during the hours when regulations applicable to such curb
loading zone are effective and then only for a period not to exceed three (3)
minutes. (Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-14: OFF-STREET PARKING AND LOADING:
Refer to
title XI, chapter 12 of this Code. (Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-15: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS:
The provisions of this chapter prohibiting the standing or parking of any
vehicle shall apply at all times or at those times herein specified or as
indicated on official signs except when it is necessary to stop a vehicle to
avoid conflict with other traffic or in compliance with the direction of a
police officer or official traffic-control device. (Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-16: REGULATIONS NOT EXCLUDED:
The provisions of this chapter imposing a time limit on parking shall not
relieve any person from the duty to observe other and more restrictive
provisions prohibiting or limiting the stopping, standing or parking of
vehicles in specific places or at specified times. (Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-17: AUTHORITY TO REMOVE VEHICLES:
If any City police officer, or any employee or agent of the City, charged with
the responsibility of repairing, cleaning, clearing, maintaining, protecting,
regulating traffic on, sweeping or plowing City streets, encounters a vehicle
parked unlawfully on any posted street, that officer or employee or agent shall
have the authority to remove said vehicle, or contact some people or agency or
firm capable of removing said vehicle. (Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-18: VEHICLE DAMAGED DURING REMOVAL, NONLIABILITY:
Any person authorized by this chapter to remove a parked vehicle, or that
person's designee, shall not be responsible for any damage done to the vehicle
during its removal, unless said damage is done intentionally, wilfully or as a
result of gross negligence. The City shall not be liable for any damage done to
any vehicle under any circumstances, nor shall the City be liable for any
damage or injury to any person or property if said damage was incurred as a
result of moving any vehicle, parked in violation of this chapter. (Ord. 192,
5-15-1989)
6-9-19: LIABILITY FOR TOWING AND STORAGE CHARGES:
Any person called upon by any officer or employee authorized to act pursuant to
this chapter to remove a parked vehicle shall have a lien against said vehicle
until all towing and storage charges are paid and satisfied in full by the
owner thereof. (Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-20: CITY NOT LIABLE:
No officer, employee, agent, nor the City shall incur any liability from any
act arising from any person's failure to remove any vehicle parked in violation
of this chapter. (Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-21: REQUEST VEHICLE REMOVAL BY OWNER:
The City shall have the authority to request that the owner, possessor, holder,
bailee, user or person in control of any vehicle parked on any City street move
the vehicle, when that vehicle impedes the performance of the supplying of any
Municipal service, to enable City crews to maintain, plow, clean, alter or
repair said street, or to perform any and all Municipal services as said
services may become necessary. (Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-22: REFUSAL TO REMOVE VEHICLE:
Should any police officer or city employee make any request to any person
listed in section
6-9-21 of this chapter, and should that person by word or action refuse to
remove said vehicle after the request, the officer or city employee shall have
the authority to summon assistance and remove the vehicle at the owner's
expense. The officer or city employee authorized to make the request, or his
designee, shall not be responsible for any damage done to the vehicle during
its removal. (Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-23: LIEN AGAINST VEHICLE:
Any person removing such a vehicle at the request of any person authorized to
make the request shall have a lien against the vehicle as provided for in
section
6-9-19 of this chapter. (Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-24: REMOVAL BY CITY:
Should a city police officer or employee, after diligent inquiry, be unable to
locate any person who shall accept the responsibility of moving a vehicle which
the officer or employee determines needs to be moved, the officer or employee
shall have the authority to summon assistance and remove the vehicle at the
owner's expense without incurring liability for his actions. Any persons acting
on behalf of the city shall have the same lien rights as set forth above. (Ord.
192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-25: VEHICLES OBSTRUCTING EMERGENCY CITY SERVICES:
Should any parked vehicle, attended or unattended, impede, delay or obstruct
any police officer, any emergency vehicle or any municipal employee rendering
or attempting to render any emergency service at any time, the officer, driver
of the emergency vehicle, or employee offering emergency services shall have
the authority to remove the obstructing vehicle without notice or without any
attempt to notify the owner or any person in control of the vehicle. This
section shall not be construed as limiting any common law rights of officers or
persons rendering emergency services, but shall be construed as an additional
grant of authority. (Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
6-9-26: PARKING OR CAMPING:
It is unlawful for any person to park any travel or camp trailer, tent or motor
home on any street, alley or highway or other public place, or on any tract of
land owned by any person occupied or unoccupied within the city except as
provided in this section as follows:
(A)   No person shall park, place or locate and use any travel or camp trailer,
tent or motor home for human habitation or for any other purpose on any street,
alley or highway or other public place, lot, tract or parcel of land in the
city except in a licensed trailer court or other facility licensed or
authorized for such purposes. The use of the Payette County Fairgrounds for
purposes authorized by the Payette County Fair Board is hereby expressly exempt
from the provisions of this section.
(B)   The parking of any unoccupied travel or camp trailer or motor home in any
accessory private garage or other suitable enclosure or in the side or rear
yard of a lot or property in any zone that allows such parking is hereby
expressly permitted.
(C)   A temporary permit may be issued to any non-resident person to be a
tourist or visitor, which will permit such person to park his/her travel
trailer, camp trailer or motor home upon a lot, tract or parcel of land in a
residential zone for a period not to exceed fourteen (14) days; provided
however, the permit shall be affixed to the vehicle in a conspicuous place on
the street side thereof; and provided further that such temporary permit shall
be issued only upon satisfactory evidence that proper sanitary facilities are
available. Such temporary permit shall require a fee as established by
resolution of the city council to be paid at the time the permit is issued.
Such permits may only be issued to persons visiting a resident within the city
of New Plymouth and such person must provide proof that the applicant for the
permit is a non-resident.
(D)   For purposes of this section, a person who owns or leases property in the
city of New Plymouth shall not be deemed a "non-resident".
(E)   A travel or camp trailer or motor home may be parked on a street or any
alley for a period of time not to exceed forty-eight (48) hours for the
purposes of loading and unloading; provided however that such parking shall not
obstruct access or travel on the street or in the alley. Under no circumstances
shall a travel or camp trailer or motor home be used for human habitation
during such periods of loading and unloading.
(F)   The provisions of this section shall not apply or affect new or used
trailer houses, travel or camp trailers, or motor homes for sale, stored or
placed on trailer sales lots, that have been established under proper permit
and license from the city and are otherwise subject to the regular building and
zoning provisions of the city.
(G)   A criminal misdemeanor citation to enforce a violation of the provisions
of this Section may be issued immediately by an appropriate law enforcement
officer. Civil enforcement of the provisions of this section shall require a
notice of abatement to be served upon the owner of the travel or camp trailer
or motor home forty eight (48) hours prior to any action (such as removal,
commencement of civil process or any other action) to enforce the provisions of
this section.
(H)   Any appropriate law enforcement officer shall order any person
habituating a travel or camp trailer or motor home to vacate said premises or
shall order the removal of a travel or camp trailer or motor home by serving a
notice of abatement as provided in subsection G of this section on the owner
thereof or by posting such notice on said travel or camp trailer or motor home.
   If said travel or camp trailer or motor home is not removed within the time
so fixed, the Police Chief or his authorized representative may cause said
travel or camp trailer or motor home to be removed and the actual costs of
removal, towing and storage shall be charged to the owner for as long as the
travel or camp trailer or motor home are in the possession and custody of the
city. If the owner fails to claim, retake possession and pay all costs as set
forth by this subsection within thirty (30) days of the city taking possession,
the city shall have the right to sell the travel or camp trailer or motor home
in order to recover the costs of taking possession.
(I)   In addition to the civil remedies provided by this section, violation of
the provisions of this section shall constitute a misdemeanor. (Ord. 245, 4-20-
1998; Ord. 394, 7-9-2019)
6-9-27: VIOLATIONS:
Each violation of this chapter shall be a misdemeanor. (Ord. 192, 5-15-1989)
CHAPTER 10
PUBLIC NUISANCE
SECTION:
6-10-1: Public Nuisance Defined
6-10-2: Public Nuisance, Unequal Damage
6-10-3: Reserved
6-10-4: Reserved
6-10-5: Specific Actions Or Conditions, Public Nuisances
6-10-6: Additional Powers
6-10-7: Violation; Penalty
6-10-8: Abatement
6-10-9: Additional Rights Of Abatement
6-10-10: Remedies Not Exclusive
6-10-1: PUBLIC NUISANCE DEFINED:
Anything which is injurious to health, or is indecent, or offensive to the
senses, or an obstruction to the free use of property, so as to interfere with
the comfortable enjoyment of life or property by an entire community or
neighborhood, or by a considerable number of persons, or unlawfully obstructs
the free passage or use, in the customary manner, or any canal, basin, or any
public park, square, street or highway, is a public nuisance. (Ord. 349, 5-2-
2016)
6-10-2: PUBLIC NUISANCE, UNEQUAL DAMAGE:
An act which affects an entire community or neighborhood, or any considerable
number of persons, as specified in the last section, is not less a nuisance
because the extent of the annoyance or damage inflicted upon individuals is
unequal. (Ord. 349, 5-2-2016)
6-10-3: RESERVED:
(Ord. 349, 5-2-2016)
6-10-4: RESERVED:
(Ord. 349, 5-2-2016)
6-10-5: SPECIFIC ACTIONS OR CONDITIONS, PUBLIC NUISANCES:
Any of the following actions, omissions or conditions which exist or which may
be allowed to exist are declared to be public nuisances:
   (A)   Allowing any number or amount of household appliances, furnishings,
fixtures, accessories, supplies or equipment to accumulate and remain for more
than seven (7) days outside of a building or permanent enclosure.
   (B)   Allowing discarded or junk items to accumulate in any manner which
creates an unsightly appearance.
   (C)   Allowing any amount of garbage to accumulate upon any premises.
   (D)   Allowing any items to be permanently stored upon any premises outside
of a permanent structure. Evidence that an item has remained unused or unmoved
for a period of one hundred eighty (180) days shall be evidence of permanent
storage.
   (E)   Allowing any condition to exist which would create any type of fire
hazard.
   (F)   Allowing weeds, grasses or bushes to grow in a tall or unsightly
manner.
   (G)   Allowing buildings to become rundown or to fall into such a state of
disrepair as to constitute an unsightly appearance, a fire hazard, or an
attractive nuisance; or which would fall into such a state of disrepair as to
create a hazard of any sort.
   (H)   Allowing a vacant building to be used for any immoral or illegal
purposes.
   (I)   Storing, accumulating or allowing any amount of junk, unused or
discarded materials adjacent to any schoolhouse, church, public park, public
grounds, business buildings or a residence without first providing proper and
tight buildings for the storage of the same. (Ord. 349, 5-2-2016)
6-10-6: ADDITIONAL POWERS:
This list of specific nuisances shall not be construed as in any way limiting
the definition of a public or moral nuisance, either within this chapter or at
common law, but shall be construed as powers enumerated in addition to those
conferred by the general definition or at common law. (Ord. 349, 5-2-2016)
6-10-7: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person who violates this chapter or commits any act or who allows any
condition to exist which is a violation of this chapter, or who by reason of a
landlord-tenant relationship, or as owner of said property aids in the
commission of any act which is a violation of this chapter, or who by reason of
any of the above set out relationships can require the owner or occupant to
cease any action which is in violation of this chapter, but fails to do so,
after acquiring knowledge of the existence of said condition shall be guilty of
a misdemeanor, punishable by one year in the Payette County Jail or by a fine
of one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) or by both such fine and imprisonment.
Every day any condition is allowed to exist which is in violation of this
chapter shall be a distinct and separate offense. (Ord. 349, 5-2-2016)
6-10-8: ABATEMENT:
If any condition is allowed to exist which is defined as a nuisance pursuant to
any section of this code, public, private, moral or otherwise, the city may
proceed to abate the same.
   (A)   If the city finds any public, private or moral nuisance to exist as
defined by Idaho Code or by any of the above sections, the city may without
notice, criminally prosecute the owners or occupants of the buildings in which
the public, private or moral nuisance is found to exist; in addition, the city
may seek injunction relief to permanently enjoin any further conduct or actions
which would constitute a public, private or moral nuisance.
   (B)   Should the director of public works, the building inspector, any
member of the city's designated law enforcement agency or any other person
designated by the mayor or city council, find any nuisance to exist, they shall
cause notice to be sent to the owner, caretaker or occupant of the premises
advising said person or persons of the nature of the nuisance. Said notice
shall be sent by regular mail and shall state the nature of the nuisance. The
notice shall advise said person or persons that the nuisance must be abated
within ten (10) days from the date of notice. Notice shall be complete upon the
date of mailing. If within ten (10) days from the date of mailing the nuisance
has not been abated, the city shall have the right, without further notice, to
enter the premises, abate the nuisance, and bill the occupant or landowner. If
payment is not forthcoming, the city shall have the right within ninety (90)
days to file a lien against said property for the value of services provided.
The city shall further have the right to foreclose its lien against said
property and include as a lienable item, all court costs, attorney fees, costs
of notice and all incidental costs. The city shall retain all rights of action
in addition to those provided herein. Nothing in this section shall preclude
the city from filing criminal actions without notice, for violations hereof.
   (C)   The city's right to abate any nuisance shall include, but not be
limited to, the following rights:
      1.   To enter upon real property and remove any item, or vehicle bodies
listed in subsections
6-10-5(A) through (I) of this chapter.
      2.   To remove or demolish any object, building, thing or condition which
would constitute a fire hazard.
      3.   To cut and remove any weeds or grasses allowed to grow in a tall or
unsightly manner.
      4.   To board up, demolish, repair, tear down or remove any building
which has fallen into such a state of disrepair so as to have an unsightly
appearance, or
      5.   To take any steps necessary to keep persons from entering into
vacant buildings for immoral or illegal purposes. (Ord. 349, 5-2-2016)
6-10-9: ADDITIONAL RIGHTS OF ABATEMENT:
This list shall not be deemed as an enumeration of all the rights of abatement,
nor as limiting the city in any manner nor as an exhaustive list of abatement
rights, but shall be construed as providing rights in addition to any other
rights of abatement provided by statute or at common law. (Ord. 349, 5-2-2016)
6-10-10: REMEDIES NOT EXCLUSIVE:
The remedies in this chapter shall not be deemed exclusive remedies, but may be
pursued individually, separately or jointly or concurrently. (Ord. 349, 5-2-
2016)
CHAPTER 11
GARAGE SALES
SECTION:
6-11-1: Definition
6-11-2: Permits Required
6-11-3: Written Permit
6-11-4: Permit Fees
6-11-5: Permit Conditions
6-11-6: Display Of Permit
6-11-7: Revocation And Refusal Of Permit
6-11-8: Hours Of Operation
6-11-9: Display Of Sale Property
6-11-10: Advertising Signs
6-11-11: Appeals
6-11-12: Penalty
6-11-1: DEFINITION:
"Garage sale" shall mean and include all general sales open to the public,
conducted from or on any residential premises in any residential zone, for the
purpose of disposing of personal property including, but not limited to, all
sales entitled "garage", "lawn", "yard", "attic", "porch", "room", "backyard",
"patio", or "moving". This definition shall not include a sale where no more
than five (5) specific items are held out for sale and all advertisement for
such sale specifically names those items to be sold. For purposes of this
definition of "garage sale", personal property shall mean property which is
utilized, owned and maintained by an individual or by members of his residence
and acquired in the normal course of living in or maintaining a residence. It
does not include merchandise which was purchased for resale or obtained on
consignment. (Ord. 254, 7-19-1999)
6-11-2: PERMITS REQUIRED:
No garage sale shall be conducted unless and until the individual desiring to
conduct said sale shall obtain a permit therefor from the City. Multiple-
resident garage sales shall be allowed under one permit, but shall be limited
to or conducted at the residence of one resident named in the permit. (Ord.
254, 7-19-1999)
6-11-3: WRITTEN PERMIT:
Permits shall require the following information:
   (A)   Full name and address of applicant.
   (B)   The location/address at which the proposed garage sale is to be held.
   (C)   The date, or dates upon which the sale is to be held.
   (D)   An affirmative statement the property to be sold was owned by the
applicant, was owned as applicant's personal property and was neither acquired
nor consigned for the purpose of resale.
